Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Plans to Change 111

Method of Measuring Earth Silk Inspection 112

Gray Silk, Gray Warp, and Earth Silk from Zhejiang, Anhui, and Other Provinces Exempted from Inspection

Silk from Qi Li Warp and Factories in Sichuan, Hubei, and Shandong Inspected for Public Weight

Article 3 of the Detailed Rules for Silk Inspection of the Raw Silk Inspection Office of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau stipulates that all raw silk exported from Shanghai to foreign countries must be reported for inspection and public weight, and a certificate must be issued before customs declaration and export is allowed. Before the implementation of the detailed rules in April of this year, earth silk merchants and the Shanghai Export Silk Industry Association said that the situation of earth silk was complicated and the inspection and public weight might cause many obstacles. They repeatedly requested a postponement, and the bureau forwarded the request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consider the commercial situation and instructed to approve it. In the past two months, the New York Silk Association of America and the Lyon Silk Association of France have repeatedly sent letters and telegrams recognizing that the inspection and public weight of the Raw Silk Inspection Office of the bureau are very accurate and can be used as a basis for bilateral trade. The Shanghai Export Silk Industry Association has also repeatedly sent letters showing its approval and recognizing the merits of the public weight system, and has repeatedly requested that all raw silk and raw openings be forced to be inspected for public weight as soon as possible. However, earth silk has many types and complex situations, and it is difficult to test the public weight of a part of earth silk. The bureau plans to divide various earth silks into three categories: (1) Gray silk and gray warp silk are of poor quality and will change color or rot after baking, making it impossible to test for public weight. (2) The soil silk from Zhejiang, Anhui, Shandong, Sichuan, Hubei, and other provinces is made using traditional methods without the use of new heavy shaking methods. The skeins are too large and it is impossible to sample in accordance with the world's silk sampling rules. The bureau's raw silk inspection and public weight equipment cannot be applied and it is inconvenient to test for public weight. Countries around the world have never had a precedent for mandatory inspection and public weight for the above two types of earth silk. It is planned to exempt them from inspection from August 1, regardless of public weight or net weight. When transporting them abroad, the bureau will issue an exemption certificate for customs declaration and export without any charge. (3) For silk from Qi Li Warp and factories in Sichuan, Hubei, and Shandong, its quality is not inferior to that of factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and its reeling is the same as that of factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. According to the purpose of inspection, it should not be placed in the ranks of soil silk. It is planned to inspect for public weight from August 1. Once the above methods are approved, the previously announced detailed rules for raw silk inspection must also be revised. The bureau has added revisions to the points that should be changed and submitted them to the ministry for approval. Now, it is instructed that the proposal to exempt grey silk, grey warp, and traditional silk from Zhejiang, Anhui, Shandong, Sichuan, Hubei, and other provinces from inspection, regardless of net weight or public weight, from August 1, and to inspect silk from Qi Li Warp and factories in Sichuan, Hubei, and Shandong for public weight from August 1, should be approved and the detailed rules should be revised and re-ordered to be followed.

Recent News on Agricultural Product Inspection 113

Preparing to Inspect Wheat Quality

And Various Agricultural Product Pests and Diseases

The Shanghai Agricultural Product Inspection Office of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining has been established for more than a year and a half. The inspection of man-made fertilizers has achieved considerable results, and the inspection and improvement of silkworm species have also been carried out in accordance with the regulations and have been reported in various newspapers. Now, Director Jin Wensi of the office has moved to No. 141 Tiantong Road near the Bund because the original address on Xinmin Road in Zhabei was inconvenient for transportation, and is actively preparing for the following three things: (1) Inspect wheat quality. There are many flour mills in Shanghai, and a lot of wheat is sold. Domestic farmers and vendors often have the bad habit of mixing water and mud. Not only does the manufacturer have problems with the machine after purchasing, but it is also unsanitary. Therefore, many manufacturers in Shanghai compete to purchase imported wheat, and the sales of domestic wheat are decreasing day by day. In order to improve the quality of wheat, Director Jin plans to inspect the northern production area first. He has now prepared the inspection trial method and submitted it to the ministry for approval. Once the ministry order is approved, the inspection can be started. (2) Inspect various agricultural product pests and diseases. Regarding the inspection of agricultural product pests and diseases, the office has jointly with the Guangzhou Agricultural Inspection Office prepared inspection methods and submitted them to the ministry for approval and publication. The ministry has also sent insect specialist Zhang Jingeo to prepare for this matter. Now, the preparations for the inspection have already begun. It is learned that the agricultural products that should be inspected for pests and diseases include livestock hair leather, meat, aquatic products, bees, fruits, flowers, seedlings, seeds, medicinal materials, wood, cotton products, and tobacco leaves. There are many types and it is planned to implement them in order of urgency and importance. (3) Food rice registration. The office previously received a ministry order transferring the resolution of the Central Political Conference to handle the import, export, and transit of food in Shanghai. It immediately actively prepared for it and is now generally ready. However, food registration is slightly different from the inspection of morning products and the improvement of agricultural properties in regulating people's food. The office has specially added a special affairs section to handle food registration matters, and it is heard that it has been submitted to the ministry and forwarded to the Executive Yuan for approval, and the inspector Jiang Hanluo has been appointed as the acting chief of the section, and the registration can be started soon.

Relief for Chinese Cigarette Factories 114

The Municipal Government Submits to the Executive Yuan for Approval. Recently, due to the surge in gold prices and increased costs, Chinese cigarette factories are on the verge of bankruptcy. The industry association convened an emergency meeting and resolved three relief measures, which were telegraphed to the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Industry, Commerce, and Finance for approval. However, no instructions have been received. A request was submitted to the Municipal Government for forwarding. The Municipal Government, after reviewing the submission, acknowledged the truthfulness of the situation and specially submitted it to the Executive Yuan for instruction and compliance. The original submission is recorded below:

Submission for forwarding matters: The Municipal Chinese Cigarette Factory Association submits a request. Chinese cigarette manufacturers heavily rely on American leaf tobacco to cater to social needs. Three years ago, the US dollar exchange rate was approximately 70 Shanghai taels per hundred. Recently, the rate has plummeted to between 34 and 35 taels. The surge in gold prices has broken all previous records, increasing costs by more than double. Increasing prices is restricted by tax brackets, and the price increase is insufficient to cover the six levels of cigarette tax. Ceasing production would harm the livelihood of workers, and worker unemployment would impact social stability. Chinese cigarette merchants today are in a situation where they cannot make a living if they advance and cannot cease production if they retreat, reaching a dead end. On the sixth of this month, the association convened an emergency meeting and resolved three relief measures, which were telegraphed to the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Finance and Industry and Commerce for approval. No instructions have been received to date. If the government approves the relief, there is still hope for survival; otherwise, the remaining dozens of cigarette factories and tens of thousands of employed cigarette factory workers will inevitably become the next Nanyang Changxing within a year. This can be definitively stated. Representatives have been jointly dispatched by various factories to petition. We implore our mayor to provide unanimous assistance in forwarding the petition to the Executive Yuan, approving and accommodating the three relief measures telegraphed on the same day. Then, our Chinese cigarette industry can barely survive and temporarily retain a glimmer of hope. The pain is skin-deep, and life and death are at stake. We urgently and imprecisely express ourselves, hoping for understanding and consideration.

According to the petition submitted by the association representatives accompanied by the employees of various cigarette factories, the Municipal Government dispatched personnel to receive them and instructed them to await the forwarding of the petition and discuss relief measures for further compliance. It was verified that the claimed surge in gold prices and the sharp increase in costs, as well as the restriction on increasing prices due to tax brackets and the harm to workers' livelihoods from ceasing production, are indeed factual circumstances. Proper relief measures must be carefully considered to maintain the current situation. In addition to separate consultations with the Ministries of Finance, Industry, and Commerce, and instructions, the matter is reasonably forwarded for your review. It is requested that the three relief measures telegraphed by the association on the same day be approved for relief, and that instructions be followed for public convenience. Respectfully submitted.

Wu Kunshan Assassinated 117

Body Found in Xujiahui. It Seems There Has Been a Major Stimulation Recently.

Around 7:00 AM yesterday morning, a male corpse was discovered in the wilderness of Zhongshan Road near Xujiahui Xilonghua. Upon receiving a report from the villagers, the Sanjiaodi Police Station of the Second Precinct of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau dispatched police to investigate. They found a bullet wound between the temples of the deceased, entering from the left and exiting from the right. The deceased was wearing a white Xiangyun gauze long gown, white silk short shirt and trousers, black silk stockings, and black gauze shoes. He had a bald head and an eight-character-style mustache. Several business cards were found in his pocket, some of which bore the name "Wu Kunshan," identifying the deceased as Wu Kunshan, also known as Yu Ke, from Xuzhou. He resided at No. 19 Shengping Lane, Zilaihu Street, French Concession, and was 49 years old. He previously served as a battalion commander and magistrate in the military during Li Houji's time in Fujian. He resigned three years ago and came to Shanghai, where he had many friends. According to inquiries made by the Public Security Bureau to the villagers near the scene of the incident, two gunshots seemed to have been heard in the wilderness around 8:00 PM the previous night, and a car was seen speeding away. Unfortunately, no attention was paid. Wu himself left home around 6:00 PM the afternoon before, accompanied by his concubine, to play mahjong at a friend's house. He then went out alone and did not return late at night, causing his family to panic. It was not until yesterday morning that they learned of his death. The Dibao of the 28th Bao and 18th Tu reported to the court for an inspection, and Prosecutor Liu arrived at the scene and verified that Wu Kunshan had indeed died from a gunshot wound. He ordered a temporary burial and an investigation into the murder. Wu's wife and concubine, Li and Wang, and his married son, Kong Zhao, lived with Wu. However, the deceased had been acting abnormally recently and seemed to have been greatly stimulated. Post Office Driver.

Shen A'fa Drowns Himself 118

Too Much Gambling and Too Many Debts. A Suicide Note Expresses Regret.

Shen A'fa, a 28-year-old from Ningbo, had been a car driver at the local General Post Office for seven years. He had always been diligent in his work and lived with his wife, Li, in Shanghai. The couple had a good relationship. Last November, Li returned to Suzhou to visit relatives and did not return until over a month later. During this time, A'fa accepted an invitation from a friend and began frequenting major gambling establishments in Shanghai, gradually developing a bad habit. He often did not come home at night, and he continued to deceive his wife, Li. Although Li knew some clues, there was nothing she could do. On the first day of this month (Monday), A'fa was on the early shift. He got up at 5:00 AM, put on his uniform, and went to the office to take over the shift. He returned home at 12:30 PM, where Li had prepared lunch. Unexpectedly, A'fa claimed that he wanted to go to a friend in Nanshi to retrieve 100 yuan. He did not eat lunch and changed into casual clothes before leaving. He instructed Li to expect him to return home for dinner. Li was reassured, but she waited in vain until late at night, suspecting that he was wandering around outside. After leaving home, A'fa, feeling unable to face others due to the excessive money he had lost gambling over the years, boarded the Xinjiangtian wheel from Shanghai to Ningbo around 4:00 PM on July 1st. The ship weighed anchor around 5:00 PM. Around 1:00 AM, A'fa asked a waiter on the ship if Dadai ocean had been passed. The waiter replied that it had not. A'fa returned to bed and slept quietly. Around 4:00 AM, while the ship's passengers were sound asleep, A'fa, wearing only a undershirt, was told that Dadai ocean had been passed. He walked to the back of the cabin and was not seen again. A search of the ship found nothing. However, a pair of shoes was left on the rear of the cabin, and a passenger said that he saw a shadow on the water early in the morning, but it disappeared in an instant. A thorough investigation was conducted when the ship arrived at Zhenhai and Ningbo, but no one was found. Later, the waiter found two suicide notes on the ship, one addressed to his wife and one addressed to his post office colleague, Wang A'gen, a photo, a post office car permit, and several pieces of clothing. Another piece of paper stated that the waiter should deliver them to Wang A'gen for forwarding.

Suicide Note One: To my virtuous wife, know that I have no choice but to walk this last path. From now on, you must take care of everything in the family and the children. If any outsiders come to collect debts, you must arrange things properly. From now on, it will be difficult for me to see you again. I owe you money, and I can only apologize to you. In the future, if anyone from the bureau comes, show them this letter. If there are any of my clothes that are returned to the bureau, please ask virtuous wife to go to Mr. Wang A'gen at the bureau once and tell them that your husband's money has nothing to do with my woman. He is currently of unknown life or death, and you must ask everyone to be understanding. I know I am sorry for you, so I am walking this last path. Life in this world is like a dream, and everything should not be taken too seriously. A gold watch pawn ticket is enclosed in the letter. Take care of your own body and take care of the child. The rent on the house is up this month, and everything must be arranged properly by yourself. No more to say. If there are any favors from friends and relatives, I will repay them in the next life. Pray that you take care of your body. Husband, the fifth day of the sixth month.

Suicide Note Two: To Mr. Wang A'gen, I have too much debt to others and cannot think of a way to solve it, so I have to leave. The people who are owed money will ask my woman for it. My woman is a weak woman and does not understand outside affairs. Please ask Mr. Tian at the bureau to find a way to help her with other matters. I have no choice but to leave. Please take care of everything. No more to say, I wish you a happy summer. Shen A'fa kowtows, the fifth day of the sixth month. Murder.

Lunatic Sentenced Yesterday 119

Sentenced to 18 Years Imprisonment.

The lunatic Zhang Jiazhen killed a woman, Wu Zhou, and a boy, Leng Cui Bao, and injured another boy in Tianfuli, Zhonghua Road, Xiaonanmen. After being arrested by the police and receiving medical treatment, he was transferred to the local court. After investigation, the prosecutor filed charges of two counts of murder and one count of attempted murder. However, due to Zhang Jiazhen's mental incapacitation, he requested a reduced sentence. After repeated reviews and debates by the Criminal Court, Judge Zhao opened the court yesterday morning at 11:00 AM and announced the sentence after ordering Zhang Jiazhen to be brought to the court. Zhang Jiazhen was sentenced to two terms of eight years imprisonment for the two counts of murder and four years imprisonment for the attempted murder, to be served concurrently for a total of 18 years. The number of days of detention prior to the final judgment will be counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. After the sentencing, Zhang Jiazhen was asked if he accepted the 18 years of imprisonment. Zhang replied that he had no quarrel with the deceased and that it was God who told him to kill them. The official said that if he did not accept the judgment, he could file an appeal within ten days after receiving the judgment. He was then ordered to be returned to custody. Over Ten Thousand Gold Missing 120

No Remittance from Cuba Ever Received. Lawsuit Against Zhong Ruju in Shanghai Unsuccessful.

Over a dozen Cantonese people, including Tang Zheng Ying, Huang Ren Yi, Li Ju Yun, Huang Xuan Zhao, etc., were laborers in the Awanna region of Cuba. Over the course of time, their wages and hard-earned income accumulated to over ten thousand gold. In March and April of the fifteenth year, the Chinese-owned Xin Shenglong Money Exchange was tasked with remitting the funds to China. The money was to be drawn from the Liangxin Bank in Hong Kong. The bank was the Hong Kong branch of Xin Shenglong. Its nature was like a joint firm. Later, Tang and the others took the remittances back to China to redeem them in Hong Kong, but they were not redeemed. The remittances were returned to Cuba, and Xin Shenglong had already closed. Liangxin Bank then shut down as well, and Tang's funds never arrived. Recently, it was learned that the manager of Xin Shenglong, Zhong Ruju, a Cantonese native, was operating a printed paper company in Shanghai. Huang Dingzhi was selected to be the representative to come to Shanghai and hire a lawyer to file a criminal complaint with the Special District Court against Zhong for fraudulently obtaining money by falsely establishing an organization and also requested a judgment to repay the 11,900+ Hong Kong dollars and 1,376+ US dollars in civil litigation. The defendant Zhong Ruju also hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to defend, saying that the plaintiff Huang Dingzhi was not a creditor, so he did not qualify to file the lawsuit. The owner of Xin Shenglong Money Exchange was Zhong Qunying, and he had a license from the Cuban Registration Bureau as evidence. The victim had once been the manager of Xin Shenglong, but he had resigned in the fifteenth year. His successor was Liang Chuanfa. The plaintiff's lawsuit for fraud took place after the defendant resigned, so he naturally bore no responsibility. Furthermore, the defendant did not issue remittances in March and April of the fifteenth year, so the evidence could be checked. Based on the above reasons, he requested that the case be dismissed. After several hearings and examinations by Judge Cheng Shangfeng, it was concluded that the plaintiff's lawsuit against Zhong Ruju was not established. Yesterday, Zhong Ruju was declared innocent and released.

Throwing Bombs after Failed Extortion. Five Gang Members Arrested and Convicted Separately.

Gangsters Liang Guihong, Du Jingbo, Chen Hanting, Li Qing, He Yaozhou, and others from Guangdong, along with Liang You and others at large, organized the Tianfeng Society gang and established their headquarters in the East Asia Hotel in the Public Concession. Request for Release Denied 122

Fourteen-Year Sentence for Wife Murder. Already Ten Years in Prison.

Seriously Ill and Requests Release. Examination Results Not Approved.

The Greek George Coporosis killed his wife in Shanghai on July 26 of the tenth year of the Republic of China and was sentenced to fourteen years of imprisonment by the former Mixed Court on October 13 of the same year. He was sent to the West Prison on Xiamen Road to serve his sentence, and he has already been there for ten years. The prisoner is now fifty-two years old. He has contracted a disease in prison and treatment has not been effective. According to the Western doctor, he needs long-term treatment. Therefore, the Western warder of the prison reported to the patrol officer, who brought the prisoner from the prison to the Special District Court yesterday morning to request that the remainder of his sentence be suspended. Judge Cheng Shangfeng opened the court for interrogation. George stated that he had been in prison for nine years and that he had been suffering from serious illnesses in his waist and chest in recent years, causing his nerves to weaken. The doctor diagnosed that his illness was incurable and that he could only drink a little milk and eat a little bread every day. There were three other prisoners in his cell, and he could not sleep peacefully at night, which made him feel even more pain. He said that he regretted committing the crime of murder in the past and requested leniency and release. Tears streamed down his face. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang said that the defendant's serious illness had been confirmed by the Director of the Municipal Council Health Bureau and that he intended to request that the remainder of his sentence be suspended. The prisoner had been suffering from illness and had torn up his bed sheet and made it into a long strip to hang himself on the morning of the 11th of last month. The Western guards in charge of the prison found him and quickly rescued him. The prison warden asked him why he hanged himself, and he said that because he was suffering from illness, the Health Bureau had intended to release him twenty months ago, but this had not happened. In addition, because there was no appeal body, he could not appeal at the time, which led to his imprisonment. It was found that the prisoner had attempted suicide more than once since entering prison. The Municipal Council had made the same request during the Provisional Court period, but it had not been approved. The leaders of the Greek merchants in Shanghai had recently written to the police stating that if the prisoner could be released, they would be willing to guarantee him and send him back to his country. After his illness was cured, they would return him to the police to serve the remainder of his sentence. The prisoner would be released when his sentence was up in April of 1932. Judge Cheng then ordered the court's forensic doctor to examine the prisoner's body and report back. In the afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Cheng continued the court hearing. The forensic doctor examined the prisoner in court and said that although the prisoner had a disease, it did not pose a danger to his life. Therefore, he issued an order stating that, according to the forensic doctor's report, the prisoner had a nervous disorder, but it did not prevent him from serving his sentence, which was inconsistent with the provisions of Article 485, Paragraph 4 of the Criminal Procedure Law. The request to suspend the execution was not approved, and the prisoner was sent back to the West Prison on Xiamen Road by the police.

Land Purchase Scam 123

All Deeds Were Forged. Seller and Landlord Accused.

Local people Lu Fugen and Lu Tiansheng sold 7.5 li of land located at No. 12 Tu, No. 23 Bao, to Ningbo native Zhu Shien in December of the 16th year of the Republic for 3,500 yuan. The landlord Yang Yiwen was the intermediary and guarantor when the contract was drawn up. Yang also guaranteed that he could transfer the deed in the future. If a measurement was desired, the actual land was over 8.6 li. Zhu paid the land price but withheld 500 yuan until all procedures were completed and verified. However, more than two years have passed, and the deed has not been transferred. Despite repeated inquiries, the matter was evaded. Furthermore, Zhu later investigated and found that the land was actually only 7.5 li and did not exceed that amount. Therefore, he sued the two Lus in the Provisional Court earlier this year, requesting a judgment to enforce the contract and compensate for the losses. The two Lus repeatedly avoided being summoned, and the case is still unresolved. Last month, Zhu received a letter from Tailey Yanghang, which was transferred for deed transfer, stating that the household names Lu Chunlin and Lu Degui on the deeds submitted by the two Lus were all forged, as verified by the Municipal Land Bureau. Zhu realized that he had been scammed and hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to file a criminal complaint against the two Lus and landlord Yang Yiwen, requesting that they be punished for forging official documents and defrauding money. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide opened the court. Lawyer Chen presented the forged deeds and other documents, explained the case, and requested an investigation. He also said that the private lawsuit had already been filed separately. Zhu Shien then testified about the circumstances of purchasing the land from the defendants at the time. According to the defendant Lu Fugen, Tiansheng is my nephew and is currently studying in Hangzhou and could not be present today. These deeds were inherited from our ancestors and were not forged. Yang Yiwen's testimony was mostly evasive. Judge Feng ordered Lu Tiansheng to be summoned and rescheduled the hearing.

Rules for Rewards and Punishments for Cleaners and Janitors 125

Established by the Health Bureau. The Municipal Health Bureau yesterday drafted eleven rules for rewards and punishments for cleaners and janitors and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval and implementation. The articles are as follows: (1) In order to facilitate the assessment of the work of cleaners and janitors, encourage diligence, and eliminate slackers, the Bureau will reward, punish, and advance cleaners and janitors in accordance with these rules. (2) When cleaners and janitors come to the Bureau for service, they must submit two two-and-a-half-inch photographs of themselves, stating their name, age, place of origin, and address for inspection and registration in the cleaner roster. (3) The salary of cleaners and janitors will be ten yuan as the lowest grade. After that, those who work diligently for two years will advance one grade and receive an additional half yuan per month until the monthly salary reaches fifteen yuan. This will be handled in accordance with the methods for talent and diligence prescribed in these rules. (4) Cleaners and janitors who have been negligent in their work and have been punished or demoted within two years will not be promoted. However, those who have been commended or rewarded may offset their demerits. (5) Cleaners and janitors who request leave must first find a suitable substitute worker. However, the leave may not exceed two months in two years. Those who exceed this period will not be promoted or receive a salary increase. (6) When requesting leave or substituting, cleaners and janitors should use the leave certificate and substitute worker certificate prepared by the Bureau for examination and verification. The supervising department should also establish detailed merit and demerit books and salary increase books for detailed recording for verification. (7) Cleaners and janitors who have one of the following circumstances will be given a commendation or a major commendation once or a reward of two cents to one yuan, depending on the circumstances: (1) Those who have not requested leave in one year; (1) Those who work diligently and can often extend their working hours; (1) Those who can keep the road surface clean and free of garbage accumulation; (1) Those who have not had anyone in their section report uncleanness to the Bureau in one year. (8) Cleaners and janitors who have one of the following circumstances will be given a demerit or a major demerit once or a fine of two cents to one yuan, depending on the circumstances: (1) Those who often request leave on the pretext of illness; (1) Those who are absent without reason four times in a month; (1) Those who are lazy and arrive late or leave early; (1) Those who cannot sweep the road surface clean; (1) Those who do not empty the garbage cans daily and often have overnight accumulation; (1) Those who do not take good care of cleaning equipment, causing it to be easily damaged; (1) Those whose sections are often reported by citizens to the Bureau for uncleanness, and the report is verified to be true. (9) Cleaners and janitors who repeatedly commit offenses and do not listen to guidance will be dismissed. (10) After the implementation of these rules, cleaners and janitors who have served for more than five years and have not retired and die in service will be given a pension by the Bureau. (10) (1) These rules will be implemented from the date they are submitted to the Municipal Government for approval.

Passengers on Trains Sitting on Windows 127

Railway Bureau Advises Against It.

The police chiefs of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways yesterday issued an order to the police chiefs of each section, stating: "In order to comply with orders, the police chief, during inspections of the police in each section of the two railways last month, often saw passengers in the third- and fourth-class carriages sitting on the windows with their upper bodies exposed due to the hot weather. It is known that these people sit on the windows only to enjoy the cool breeze, but they do not know that when the train is running, the vibration may cause them to fall out of the train and endanger their lives. This is a matter of passenger safety and should be strictly prohibited. In addition to informing the Traffic Department and the Chief Inspector and distributing the order, it is urgently ordered that you comply and order your subordinates to carefully advise and dissuade passengers sitting on the windows to avoid danger."

Large School of White Fish in the Wusong River 128

The Larger Ones Weigh Over a Hundred Catties. The School is About Two or Three Miles Long.

In the Wusong River, which separates the counties of Wu and Kun in Jiangsu Province, large numbers of white fish have been found swimming in schools for several days. These fish are characterized by their pointed, round mouths and flat bodies. The larger ones weigh dozens of catties each, while the smaller ones weigh one or two catties each. These white fish only appear in the Wusong River during the summer and autumn seasons each year. The white fish that passed by the other day included large fish weighing over a hundred catties, which led the way in an orderly formation and were about two or three miles long, with the head and tail connected continuously. According to fishermen who believe in divine power, this is a white fish formation that is protected by deities. Therefore, fishermen do not dare to catch a single one of these white fish when they pass by. The French Concession the other night.

Prohibition of Lighters Extorting Fees 132

Extortion is Confirmed　　Proclamation and Abolition Imminent　　The lighters at the Shanghai docks were originally porters of the Qing Dynasty yamen. Since the revolution, this title has long been abolished, but these people still follow the old customs, employing gangs to specialize in transporting goods from civilian ships around the Yanpu South Guild Hall and Wanyu Wharf, arbitrarily extorting "tie-li" fees, often exceeding several times the regular labor costs of the merchants. Moreover, relying on their numbers, they act despotically without fixed prices. Shipping merchants Xing Zhigang and others witnessed this situation and immediately reported it, requesting the Municipal Public Security Bureau to order the water patrol team and the first district, first precinct to investigate thoroughly. It was confirmed and repeatedly prohibited on record. Unexpectedly, lighter bosses Xi Akun and Zhang Renhe continued unrepentantly, and were summoned and detained a few days ago. It is heard that the Bureau of Social Affairs also intends to jointly issue a proclamation limiting that, regardless of the type of goods, no extra fees should be extorted from the villagers beyond the regular loading and unloading charges, in order to eliminate bad habits and benefit the villagers.

Woman Conceals Mauser Pistol in Crotch 133

Yang Liangshi Privately Traffics in Firearms　　Yang Chunting, a detective of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, was patrolling the Huangpu River in a motorboat around 8 PM the other night. Upon arriving at Datong Wharf, they saw the Zhengda steamer docked there, not yet setting sail. They immediately boarded the ship to investigate. They noticed a woman in the cabin who appeared panicked upon seeing the police team, arousing suspicion. They conducted a search of her person but found no prohibited items. However, something seemed to bulge prominently in her crotch, so they examined it more closely. They found two Mauser pistols in the front of her crotch and another one in the back. The guns were wrapped in cloth and tied with rope, with the rope looped around her neck, allowing the guns to hang inside her front and back crotch. They immediately took the person and the evidence back to the team. During a preliminary interrogation by Chief Xu, the woman stated that she was Yang Liangshi, 47 years old, from Huai'an. She claimed that an unknown person entrusted her to take these items back to Jiangbei, promising her a reward of five yuan. The team leader, considering the seriousness of the offense of privately carrying firearms, ordered that a document be prepared and submitted to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for further investigation.

Love Story of a Female Worker and an Accountant 135

Through Great Hardship　　Finally Achieves Fulfillment　　Chen Linshi, a Cantonese woman residing at No. 47, Xingren Lane, Wuchang Road, Hongkou, has a daughter, Gui Bao, 29 years old, with a beautiful appearance. Due to difficult circumstances, she works in the fine yarn section of a certain yarn factory nearby. Unexpectedly, she developed a romance with Shen Yunqing, an accountant from Ningbo. Chen Linshi was unaware of this. Shen discussed with Gui Bao, "Our love is strong, and you are already pregnant. It is not good to continue our affair in secret. We should aim for a lifelong union." Gui Bao deeply agreed, and asked her foster mother, Feng, to act as a matchmaker for Shen. However, the mother refused, because Shen was not Cantonese, causing the two to be disappointed. Later, last month, they rented a house in Qingshan Lane, Airjin Road, and lived together. Linshi, after her daughter disappeared, investigated without success. While searching everywhere, one afternoon, she happened to be walking on North Shanxi Road when she saw Gui Bao carrying a copper hot water bottle. She stopped her daughter. Gui Bao, turning around and seeing her mother, was greatly alarmed. She had no choice but to go with her to the small house. As soon as they entered, she shouted, "My mother is here! Run!" Yunqing, hearing the sound, fled from the drying terrace, falling and injuring his leg, unable to get up. Linshi, seeing this, could not bear it and ordered him to be sent to Puhui Hospital for treatment first, and told Gui Bao to go back with her. Gui Bao knelt on the ground and refused, saying that she was four months pregnant. "If my mother does not allow me to marry Shen, I would rather die here!" She wept bitterly. After repeated persuasion from the neighbors, Linshi agreed on certain conditions and asked her foster mother Feng to be the matchmaker for Shen, to complete their private love and avoid scandal.

Two Men Abduct Two Girls 136

Abducted from Kunshan Area　　Near the Zhengyi Station on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, there were two men, around 20 or 30 years old, accompanied by two young girls. Because they looked flustered, they were stopped and questioned by the stationed soldiers. They were evasive in their answers. The four were detained and sent to the Kunshan County Public Security Branch stationed there. The branch chief learned that the two men had previously served as patrol leaders and police officers, but had been dismissed not long ago. They had abducted good family girls in Kunshan. Yesterday, a document was prepared and submitted to the county government for verification. In the morning, police were dispatched to escort them onto the Shanghai-Nanjing train back to Kunshan for detention and interrogation.

Attempted Robbery by Intercepted Bandits 137

Around 5 PM the day before yesterday, Inspector Su of the Sixth District Police Station in Caojiadu, Xuhui, and Detective Leader Liu Shaoqing, along with detectives Tang Bingxiang, Gan Youxin, Dai Qingyuan, and others, were patrolling the Jiaozhou Road area when they suddenly saw two men who looked flustered and were whispering to each other. Inspector Su and the others, finding their appearance suspicious, went forward to question them. The men were evasive and flustered, so they were taken back to the station. According to their confessions, one was Li Changgui, also known as Xiao Taozi, 32 years old, from Gaoyou, a day laborer living in a straw shed in Shihuiyao. The other was Wang Xunkui, also known as Xiao Erzi, 25 years old, from Funing, unemployed and living in a foreign workshop on Tokyo Road. They both confessed that they had been contacted by Da Kuaizi the day before yesterday to meet at 7 PM today in front of the Wujiaochang movie theater in Caojiadu. He had three pistols that he would distribute at that time, and they would go to rob the Wang Yiren doctor's pawnshop in Caojiadu town. They were discussing this plan when they were arrested. Inspector Su immediately disguised himself and Liu Shaoqing and others and reconnoitered the area around the movie theater. A moment later (it was exactly 6:50 PM), they saw four people standing there, looking furtive and flustered. They immediately rushed forward and apprehended all four, taking them back to the station. After being questioned separately by District Chief Ren, one of them confessed that he was Wu Qinghe, also known as Da Kuaizi, 28 years old, from Anhui, living at No. 289, Nanfu Lane. He was evasive in his testimony. Another, Sun Haizhou, 23 years old, from Yangzhou, a fruit seller living at No. 20, Dongyang Workshop, said that he was invited by Wu Qinghe to meet there. Wu Qinghe had three pistols but had not distributed them because not enough people had arrived. They were planning to rob the Wang Yiren doctor's pawnshop in town. Another, Zhang Yufa, 26 years old, from Yancheng, who pulled a rickshaw at Caojiuajiao, gave a similar testimony to Sun's. Another, Chen Zhenhong, 36 years old, from Funing, worked as a porter at the bull slaughterhouse on Kangnuotuo Road. He said that he was just walking around in front of the movie theater and was acquainted with Wu Qinghe and the others, so he stood with them, and did not know about their plan. District Chief Ren, after hearing the confessions, determined that Wu Qinghe was indeed the ringleader of the robbers, and the others were accomplices in the attempted robbery. Yesterday, he prepared a document and sent all six robbers to the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Yuan Da Sugar Warehouse Theft Solved 138

Three Criminals Apprehended and Sent to the Public Security Bureau for Interrogation　　The Yuan Da Sugar Warehouse near the Taikoo Company Wharf in Pudong was broken into last month by thieves who broke through the roof and stole nineteen bags of rock sugar, worth a considerable amount. The warehouse manager sent letters to the water and land police stations, requesting them to investigate and apprehend the culprits. The other day, detectives Zhang Chunting and Yang Jinsheng of the Third District Public Security Bureau apprehended the main criminals in the case, Yang Jinlin, Xu Laoer, and Yao Xiaomazi, in Lan Nidu. Interrogated at the district station, Yang Jinlin, 39 years old, from Anhui, with no fixed address, confessed that on a certain night last month (the date he couldn't remember), he colluded with Xu and Yao to sneak into the Yuan Da Sugar Warehouse. Xu climbed onto the roof, pried open the skylight, and he and Xu went inside, while Yao kept watch outside. They stole eighteen bags of rock sugar, each weighing forty or fifty jin. Yao hired a boat to transport them to the Bund of the French Concession and sold them to Yongtai Hao for 83 yuan. They paid 22 yuan for the boat and loading fees and spent a dozen yuan on the brothers at the Puxi wharf and 5 yuan to the water police. In the end, he and Xu Laoer each received 17.5 yuan, and the rest was used by Yao Xiaomazi. Xu Laoer, 35 years old, from Tongzhou, a day laborer living at No. 23, Diandang Lane, and Yao Xiaomazi, 34 years old, from Tongzhou, a day laborer living at No. 23, Diandang Lane, both confessed that they had conspired with Yang Jinlin to steal rock sugar from the Yuan Da Warehouse, admitting to the crime. District Chief Zhang ordered that the three criminals, Yang, Xu, and Yao, be escorted to the Public Security Bureau yesterday for interrogation.

Identification of Robbers 141

Brothers Fight, One Loses Arm and Fingers 142

Zhang Ajin and Zhang Xingbao Brawl　　Zhang Ajin and his younger brother Zhang Xingbao, locals from Hujia Muqiao in northern Shanghai, had a fight because Zhang Xingbao, being without food or clothing, borrowed one yuan from his brother Zhang Ajin. Ajin not only refused, but also beat his brother. Zhang Xingbao, in a fit of anger, fought back, grabbing his brother's testicles. Unexpectedly, Zhang Ajin grabbed a kitchen knife and hacked wildly at Xingbao, cutting off Xingbao's right arm and fingers. Xingbao, severely wounded, fell to the ground unconscious. The sentry arrived and arrested Zhang Ajin, taking him to the Third Precinct of the Fifth District. It was verified that Zhang Xingbao's injuries were very serious, and he was sent to Jisheng Hospital for treatment first. Zhang Ajin was transferred to the local court yesterday for punishment.

Important News from the Shipping Industry 143

Rush to Load Foreign Goods After the recent increase in gold prices, the Yangtze River shipping companies stopped transporting foreign goods. Recently, various foreign firms in Shanghai notified the Yangtze River companies to rush to transport the goods, saying that the prices of all foreign goods would increase in two weeks. Therefore, the Xun and Han shipping companies started loading the foreign goods stored in Shanghai for export yesterday, rushing to transport them within two weeks. This morning, the Xinningsing轮 shipped a full load of foreign goods. Price Increases for Upstream Cargoes Shanghai's six major shipping companies have agreed that the minimum bill of lading for export cargo to the Yangtze River has always been one liang. Now, the companies have agreed that from today onwards, the minimum bill of lading for upstream cargo must be two liang. All shipping companies have notified their customers.

Health Bureau's Serious Epidemic Prevention Work 145

Xiangya, Zu'an Factories Prevent Workers from Receiving Injections　　The Municipal Health Bureau Issues Letter of Reprimand Concerning Workers' Health　　When the Health Bureau dispatched doctors to the Xiangya Factory and Zu'an Electrical Weaving Socks Factory in Shanghai to give workers free epidemic prevention injections, the managers, begrudging a few minutes of work time, prevented the workers from stopping work to get the injections. The Health Bureau's epidemic prevention personnel told them that protecting workers' health would increase production capacity. The Health Bureau's encouragement of epidemic prevention injections was entirely voluntary and would not cost the factory or workers a single cent. They should not prevent workers from the opportunity to prevent disease, and reported back to the bureau. Yesterday, the bureau sent a letter of reprimand, saying, "On the first of this month, this bureau dispatched doctors to your factory to give all workers free cholera prevention injections. The workers were about to receive the injections, but your executives not only did not enthusiastically urge them to accept the injections, but instead prevented them. This kind of ignorant behavior is simply because you think that workers taking injections will take up a little over a minute or two of work time. It can be seen that your factory is excessively concerned with private profits and indifferent to workers' health. Your vision is narrow and your love for the community is weak, which is very regrettable. We will still dispatch doctors to your factory this month to give workers free cholera prevention injections. We hope that your executives can accept good advice and no longer hinder the workers from enjoying the benefits of free prevention. This is of utmost importance. This is addressed to Zu'an Electrical Weaving Socks Factory and Xiangya Factory."

Silk Weaving Industry Labor-Management Dispute 148

Municipal Government Arbitrated Yesterday　　In the Shanghai silk weaving industry, the factory owners' announcement of a wage reduction in January caused a labor-management dispute. Although the Bureau of Social Affairs repeatedly convened mediation meetings, no resolution was reached. The factory owners submitted a request for arbitration to the Municipal Government, which determined that the labor-management dispute was important and scheduled an arbitration meeting yesterday, appointing Huang Daolin as the chairman. The capital side was represented by four factories, Tiancheng, Jinhua, Youren, and Zhonghua. The labor side was represented by ten factories, Yutong, Yunlun, Fenghua, Xianghua, Meiwen, Zhenhua, Tiancheng, Jinhua, Youren, and Zhonghua. The chairman first instructed both sides to express their views. The capital side's reason was that there were over a hundred silk weaving factories in Shanghai. Because ten factories had labor unions, wages gradually increased, increasing costs and making it difficult to compete with other factories. Therefore, in January of this year, the trade association decided to reduce wages to maintain the status quo. The labor side's reason was that the cost of living was increasing day by day, and they had already been very understanding of the factory owners by not asking for a wage increase. The factory owners abruptly reduced wages to half, which was against the trend. The factory owners claimed that the wages of other factories were all small-scale family handicraft industries, which were difficult to compare. Therefore, they firmly requested the restoration of the original wages. After the chairman understood the situation, he consulted with the other committee members and advised both sides to make concessions. The arbitration decision can be sent to the trade union within days.

Bureau of Social Affairs Replies to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce　　Orders the Trade Union to Vacate the Buildings. Re-election of Committee Members for the Money Industry Market 150

The money industry market affiliated with the Ningbo Road Longqing Lane Money Industry Association is crowded with people during the morning and afternoon trading hours every day. Therefore, in the past, it was proposed to publicly elect two qualified and experienced staff members from the employees of various money banks to serve as committee members to maintain market order and resolve disputes. This has been in place for several years and has been very successful. However, the term of office for these publicly elected committee members is set at two years, and they can be re-elected consecutively. It is purely voluntary. The current committee members are Hu Gesheng of Ankangzhuang and Lu Shuchen of Shunkangzhuang. They have already served two consecutive terms, and their terms will expire again in July of this year. They should be re-elected. (According to the market rules, employees are limited to assistants. If they are promoted to assistant manager, they are no longer eligible to be market committee members or election committee members). Originally, both Hu and Lu could be re-elected, but this year, Hu was promoted to assistant manager of Yongshengzhuang, and Lu was also promoted to assistant manager of Shunkangzhuang, so neither is eligible for re-election. Therefore, new committee members must be produced in this re-election. The election is currently underway and will be announced soon.

Case of Huaheng Ship Colliding with Barge 151

Claim Filed with Insurance Company　　Three hundred bags of sorghum, which were reported by Yu Shungong on behalf of a customer, were loaded onto Zhu Guisheng's barge to be transported to the Nisshin Wharf and then transferred to the Nisshin ship Fengyang丸 for transport to the Yangtze River. The barge was berthed outside the Nisshin ship when it was hit by the Huasheng ship of the Xinhua Company, breaking Zhu Guisheng's barge in two and causing all the sorghum to fall into the water and sink. Also, twenty-eight bags of white rice in the Xingji and Niuxinglong barge berthed inside the Nisshin ship were also damaged by water. Both cargoes were insured with Taikoo and claims have been filed.

Service Rules for Female Inspectors 152

Revised and Promulgated　　The Service Rules for Female Inspectors of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau were previously submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and implementation. However, as the original rules were not entirely appropriate, they have been revised item by item and submitted to the Municipal Government. Order No. 5948 of the Municipal Government approves the Bureau to promulgate and implement the rules, which are listed below: Service Rules for Female Inspectors of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Article 1 Female inspectors are under the supervision and command of the Bureau's Duty Inspector General and are assigned to inspection duties at various ports, stations, and temporary assignments. Article 2 When performing inspection duties at the assigned location, female inspectors shall also be under the command of the director of the district station in charge of the area and the guidance of the chief inspection personnel. Article 3 After being assigned to a position, female inspectors shall serve diligently on time and shall not make excuses to ask for leave or leave their posts without permission. Article 4 Female inspectors shall first pay close attention to the passengers and pedestrians at the assigned location. If there is any suspicious situation, they shall proceed with the inspection. Article 5 Female inspectors shall perform inspection duties in conjunction with the police officers of the district station in charge or the chief inspection personnel dispatched by the Bureau within the police jurisdiction. They shall not enter the road police boundaries or military inspection locations. Article 6 Female inspectors shall conduct inspections with a kind attitude and meticulous methods and shall not speak harshly or act rudely. They shall also inform the inspected person of the reasons for the inspection in detail. Article 7 The main task of female inspectors is to inspect the bodies of women. If it is necessary to inspect luggage and other items, it shall be done in the presence of the inspected person. Article 8 Inspections shall be carried out with quick and appropriate procedures. If it is necessary to open it, the inspected person shall be instructed to open it by themselves. After the inspection, each item shall be checked and returned clearly. Article 9 If a female inspector finds prohibited items, she shall immediately send the person and the witness to the district station in charge for interrogation and shall not delay or conceal them. If there is any corruption, leniency, bribery, collusion, fraud, or false reporting, once discovered, they will be severely punished according to law. Article 10 Female inspectors shall fill out a report form every day on the inspection situation and report to the Supervision Office and the district station in charge. The wording shall be concise and not sloppy. Article 11 If there are any incomplete matters in these rules, they may be submitted for amendment at any time. Article 12 These rules shall be implemented from the date of approval and promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Minutes of the Brick and Tile Trade Association Regular Meeting 160

The Shanghai Brick and Tile Trade Association held its twelfth executive and standing committee meeting at 2 p.m. the day before yesterday. (2) Regarding whether to solicit cooperation from gray kiln vendors and grass paper/bamboo stick vendors since they are within the scope of the trade, it was decided to conduct a general registration within a limited time, following the cart and basket bearer method. Letter to the Editor 164

To the Editor of Shen Bao: With regard to the questions raised by Mr. Wang Yasheng in your newspaper's June 30th issue concerning the National Photography Exhibition, Mr. Wang has some misunderstandings, and we would like to clarify as follows: "Subscribing to a copy of the photography magazine" does not make one a member of our association. Ordinary members are required to pay an annual fee of eight yuan upon joining, while the subscription fee is only two yuan. Details are stated in the association's charter, which can be requested by mail. Regarding Mr. Wang's statement about "hiring a Westerner who falsely claims to be a member of the Royal Photographic Society of England...", Mr. Deng Tuo is indeed an "honorary" or "affiliated" member (there is no standard translation in our country) A.R.P.S. This is a fact and not a false claim. Furthermore, Mr. Deng Tuo was also a judge in last year's competition. Since the exhibition has no prizes, there is no need for judges. Mr. Wang seems to be confusing the competition with the exhibition. We are well aware that Mr. Deng Tuo is very knowledgeable about photography. "There are many Chinese photographers whose skills are higher than Deng Tuo's," please introduce them to us. We would be happy to welcome them, as our association will hold the eighth photography competition next spring. Sincerely, Secretary of the Chinese Photographic Society.

Minutes of the Sixth Meeting The China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture The total amount of funds allocated this year is 350,000 yuan. Re-election of Directors: Weng Wenhao resigns, Jin Shaoji succeeds.

Attendees 166

The China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture is an organization that manages the second installment of the Boxer Indemnity returned by the United States. Its sixth annual meeting was originally scheduled to be held in Nanjing on June 27th. However, due to the sudden illness of American Director Coolidge after arriving in Shanghai, he was unable to attend. The meeting was rescheduled to be held in Nanjing on July 2nd. The meeting was held in the Ministry of Education conference room at 9 a.m. Attending directors included Cai Yuanpei, Jiang Menglin, Hu Shi, Weng Wenhao, Ren Hongjun, Li Yu-ying, Zhao Yuanren, etc. Xu Mo, Director of the Department of European and American Affairs of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Sun Benwen, Director of the Department of Specialized Affairs of the Ministry of Education, attended as observers.

Matters Discussed 167

At 9:30 a.m., Chairman Cai Yuanpei announced the opening of the meeting. After performing the ceremony, the reports of the honorary secretary, honorary accountant, and chief of the executive committee were approved. The next discussion was the budget for various undertakings to be carried out in the next year, including: (1) science professorships, (2) compilation committee, (3) science research grants and awards, (4) social survey institute, (5) National Peiping Library, (6) Jing Sheng Biological Survey Institute, and (7) executive office, with a total expenditure of over 973,000 yuan. In addition, the association planned to establish two new undertakings: one was to conduct a national soil survey in preparation for agricultural improvement.

Science Professorships: This year, it is planned to establish one professorship each at the Geological Survey Institute of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining and the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica, requiring approximately 20,000 yuan. Therefore, the association's own undertakings would spend a total of over one million yuan. In the afternoon, the meeting continued to discuss the allocation of funds to various requesting institutions. The association received over 40 requests for funds this year, with requested amounts totaling approximately 5 million yuan. In addition to the 230,000 yuan already approved for continued subsidies from the previous year, the actual amount available for allocation was only over 300,000 yuan. The directors deliberated extensively on this subsidy, and finally decided to allocate over 350,000 yuan this year. Ministry of Education Plans to Consolidate Cultural Institutions 171

The Ministry of Education recently plans to formulate regulations for libraries, museums, educational halls, public lecture halls, and the preservation of antiquities and documents. It will also work with the Ministry of Interior to formulate regulations prohibiting the export of ancient books and antiquities and strictly enforce them. It will review the methods for examining domestic academic groups and foreign joint scientific investigation teams and formulate a plan to expand the directly-affiliated libraries and antiquities preservation institutions in phases. The above matters are all being actively planned.

Record of the Second Anhui Provincial Education Bureau Directors' Conference (1) 172

(1) Opening Ceremony: The opening ceremony of the Second Anhui Provincial Education Bureau Directors' Conference was held at 8:30 a.m. on July 1st. The details are as follows: The conference hall was the auditorium of the No. 1 Vocational School. Attendees included Provincial Government Committee members Li Fanyi (also Director of the Construction Department), Jin Weixi (also Provincial Party Member), Ma Jidi, Li Yingsheng, Zhang Keyao, Provincial Government Secretary-General Shui Zi, President of the High Court Zeng Youhao, Director of the Education Fee Management Office Cheng Xiaosu, and Provincial Party Committee member Zhang Deliu, etc. There were also approximately 200 guests from various institutions. Forty-two bureau directors attended, and twenty staff members from the Education Department attended as observers. The meeting opened at 8:30 a.m. Chairman Cheng Tianfang briefly reported on the preparation process of the conference and his hopes for the conference. Provincial Party Committee member Jin Weixi gave a speech hoping that the conference would pay attention to party-oriented education and agricultural education. Provincial Government Committee member Li Fanyi gave a speech hoping that attention would be paid to the thinking of the education community and that efforts would be made to promote rural education to prevent teachers and students from going astray. Director of the Education Fee Management Office Cheng Xiaosu gave a speech advocating that the implementation of compulsory education should be carried out in stages to avoid being merely nominal and not actually effective. Afterwards, Provincial Government Secretary-General Shui Zi, President of the High Court Zeng Youhao, and Principal of No. 1 High School Peng Jixiang gave speeches in succession. Director Representative Xu Renzhang gave a reply. The meeting adjourned at 11:30 a.m. (2) First General Assembly: The first general assembly began at 2 p.m. on the 1st. There were 62 members present. The meeting was chaired by Cheng Tianfang, Director of the Education Department, who designated Ouyang Qi, Director of the Dongliu Education Bureau, as the chairman according to the conference outline. After the meeting, the members' seats were drawn, and one vice-chairman was elected by ballot according to the outline. As a result, Luo Huitan, Director of the Shexian Education Bureau, was elected. The chairman then designated the members of the various review groups, which were divided into seven groups: educational administration, funding, compulsory education, school education, adult education, social education, and vocational education, with eight to eleven people in each group, and one person was designated as convener for each group. Afterwards, Li Zhongxiang of the agenda group of the preparatory office reported on the preparation process and the compilation of the agenda. At this point, the discussion of the agenda began. The first agenda discussed was that of the educational administration group. The results were as follows: First proposal: School districts in each county should be the same as administrative districts. It was decided to hand it over for review. The second to eighth proposals were all about holding joint examinations for primary school graduates. It was decided to combine them and hand them over for review. The ninth to twelfth proposals were all about raising the salaries of local educational administrative personnel. It was decided to combine them and hand them over for review. Thirteenth proposal: From now on, the directors of municipal and county education bureaus should be appointed from qualified personnel through examinations, abolishing the system of guarantees from the county magistrate. It was decided to hand it over for review. The discussion ended at 5:30 p.m. The meeting adjourned. In the evening, only one review group, the administrative group, held a meeting convened by Zhu Yiyu. The discussion lasted for a long time. As a result, a decision will be submitted to the fifth general assembly. In the evening at 6 p.m., the director of the Education Department invited the attendees. (3) Second General Assembly: The following is the situation on the second day of the conference, the 2nd: Change of Agenda: According to the original agenda, the funding group's agenda should be discussed today. However, since the administrative group's agenda had already discussed 13 items yesterday, and the adult, social, and vocational groups had not yet been discussed, the agenda from yesterday was continued today. Opening Ceremony: The meeting opened at 8 a.m. with Vice Chairman Luo Huitan presiding over the meeting as usual. There were 62 members present. Proposal 14: Please set up a training institute for local educational administrative personnel in the Education Department. The resolution was submitted for review. Proposal 15: Utilize the summer vacation to hold a training institute for local education workers. The resolution was submitted for review. Proposal 16: The county school inspector must have considerable knowledge and administrative experience. The proposal was withdrawn voluntarily. Proposal 17: The county school inspector should pay attention to inspection reports. The resolution was passed without discussion. Proposals 18 and 19: The county magistrate should pay attention to education, and the provincial school inspector should increase supervision. The resolution was combined and a revised proposal was made to change it to "Strictly Implement the County Magistrate's Performance Evaluation for Running Schools". The method was handed over to the review committee for drafting. Proposal 20: The provincial school inspector should continue to serve in a certain district after inspecting it. The resolution was passed. Proposals 21 and 22: To protect education workers. The resolution was passed in principle, and the method will be reviewed. Proposal 23: Unify forms. The resolution was passed. The discussion was suspended for ten minutes. Continued discussion, still following the first day's agenda, discussing the adult education group's first to 137th proposals: Please instruct the county magistrate to investigate the illiterate people. The resolution was rejected. Proposal 138: Prepare to run people's schools. The resolution was to have the proposer, Bengbu City, submit it to the department for handling. Proposals 129, 140, 141, and 3 were all about implementing adult literacy education. The resolution was to combine and submit them for review. At this time, it was already 12 o'clock, and the meeting adjourned. Afternoon Lecture: Today's afternoon from 2 to 5 p.m. was a lecture meeting. The speakers were Cheng Tianfang, Director of the Education Department, and Mao Baoheng, Principal of the No. 1 Vocational School. Evening Review: The Administrative and Adult Education Review Committees held meetings from 7 p.m. tonight. The Administrative Group was convened by Zhu Yiyu, and the Adult Group was convened by Zhang Zemin. The results of the review will be submitted to the Fifth General Assembly.

Measures to Preserve the National Sports Field 178

Build barracks on the other side of the playground Expenses will be shared equally by all officers in the same province The National Games closed on April 11th, and all field work has been rushed to completion. Sports Advancement Association Ground Temporarily Not to Be Recovered 179

Although the Rockefeller contract has expired, it can still be used for a short time. The board of directors is actively seeking another location for a permanent solution. The ground of the Labor Father Road China Sports Advancement Association, owned by the American oil magnate Rockefeller, was unconditionally lent to our country as a place to promote amateur sports. The contract expired on June 20th of this year. The Sports Advancement Association recently re-negotiated with the Rockefeller Foundation for a renewal of the loan, but the Rockefeller Foundation had to take back the land and refused to renew the loan. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now known that Dr. Yu Rizhang, Secretary-General of the National YMCA, negotiated with the Rockefeller Foundation and can still continue to use it because the land will not be used for other purposes in the next few years, nor will it be sold, and it must be preserved. According to observations by those related to the Rockefeller Foundation, although the contract for the ground has expired, it will not be recovered. However, for the sake of planning future work, the Sports Advancement Association is conducting further negotiations with the Rockefeller Foundation to determine the term of renewal, whether it is half a year or a year, so as not to hinder the undertaking of the ideal cause. The board of directors of the Advancement Association is seeking another piece of land to build its own sports ground as a fixed clubhouse. In short, the Rockefeller's land currently has no intention of being recovered, and the sports cause in this city and the whole country will not be affected. It is necessary to temporarily allocate the ground as a barracks and training ground, which will be beneficial for both preservation and custody. A request was submitted to the Executive Yuan to order the Zhejiang Provincial Government to comply. Dai Chuanxian, Chairman of the Association, believed that the construction cost of the dormitory used on the ground was huge. If it is not properly preserved, it would be a great pity. To allocate it as a military barracks would further prolong the trampling, which is definitely not the best policy. For the sake of the overall interests of both parties, three measures for disposal were formulated and submitted to the Central Government for forwarding to the Ministry of Military Affairs for notification. The three measures are recorded as follows: (1) The Zhejiang Provincial Government will delineate a piece of land outside the city equal in size to the current training ground and build barracks and training grounds. The expenses will be borne equally by the National Government and the Zhejiang Provincial Government. (2) The current sports ground will be designated as the National Hangzhou Sports Ground and handed over to the Education Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government for management. (3) Before the above construction is completed, the current sports ground will be temporarily lent to the military for use. The sports construction on the ground will be the responsibility of the Zhejiang Provincial Education Department to take care of. The above measures have been resolved by the Zhejiang Provincial Committee and the Education Department has been ordered to send personnel to take over. However, since the site will be allocated for military use before the new barracks are completed, the protection of the sports buildings on the ground is quite difficult. It seems that the ground should be demarcated and the remaining houses should be temporarily lent to the military. This method of dividing and living can take into account both military use and the maintenance of public education. This measure will be submitted by the Zhejiang Provincial Government to the Executive Yuan for an order to the Ministry of Military Affairs for joint notification.

Far East Games 180

Changes in Track and Field Events At the 9th Far East Games held in Japan in mid-May of this year, representatives of the three countries met and decided to divide the track and field events into two championships, track and field, and also made changes in the events. As a result, the 800-meter relay was cancelled and changed to a 400-meter relay (4X100), the 200-meter low hurdles were changed to 400-meter intermediate hurdles, and the twelve-pound shot put was changed to a sixteen-pound heavy item. The items are as follows: Track Championship Field Championship High Jump 100 meters Long Jump 100 meters Triple Jump 400 meters Pole Vault 800 meters Discus 1500 meters Javelin 10000 meters Sixteen-pound shot put 110 meters high hurdles 400-meter low hurdles In addition, the all-around sports championship includes five events, ten events, 400-meter relay, and 1600-meter relay. In addition, Japan proposed to add the hammer throw to the field events, but it failed to pass due to opposition from China and the Philippines, but it was allowed to be included as a performance. It is found that in the World Olympics, there is only a sixteen-pound shot put but no twelve-pound one, there are only 400-meter low hurdles but no 200-meter ones, and the relay races are 400 meters and 1600 meters but no 800-meter relay. Japan's proposal this time is completely based on the standards of the World Games, because Japan's goal is to compete in the world arena, not in the Far East Games of China, Japan, and the Philippines. The revised events are of great benefit to our country. It is deeply hoped that the sports circles of all countries will work hard to promote the Guangdong Women's Table Tennis Team.

Appointed Yu Binqi as Consultant 181

The Shanghai Guangdong Women's Table Tennis Team has been established for more than half a year. The team affairs are guided by Zeng Rongzong. The team is actively reorganized and developed rapidly. Hangzhou City Initiates Track and Field Competition 183

Using Summer Vacation to Promote Skills Competition to Start on the 11th Hangzhou News The Sports Department of the Provincial Public Education Center has aroused the interest of the whole city's public in practicing since it initiated the open competition. In order to take advantage of the summer vacation, it specially initiated the track and field competition to promote track and field skills. Registration started yesterday and will end on the 10th of this month. Regarding the qualifications for participation, anyone can register, except those who are engaged in sports. Men are divided into two groups, A and B, and women are not divided into groups. The standard for grouping is based on a height of 63 inches and a weight of 115 pounds. Those who exceed the standard are in Group A, and those who are below the standard are in Group B. The competition date is set to be held in stages after 5 pm every day starting from the 11th due to the recent hot weather. All rules will be implemented in accordance with the latest Far East Games rules. Prizes have been set to give souvenirs to the first place in each group and the top three in each event. The City No. 1 Public Stadium Amateur Tennis Competition was originally scheduled to start on the 2nd, but the weather was not good and it rained heavily, causing the athletes to have no place to show their talents. The results of yesterday's competition and the schedule for this afternoon and tomorrow morning are recorded as follows: Group Contestants Results Fang Yang Xie Mao beat Xiao Mingzu 1 to 6, 6 to 3, 9 to 7 Xiao Wu Maoqing beat Wang Keyong 2 to 6, 6 to 4, 6 to 3 Xia Shen Shounan beat Zhao Qingxiang Zhao Qingxiang abandoned the match Hao Wang Liang beat Wang Hongye 2 to 6, 6 to 3, 6 to 0 Hao Sun Chuanxin beat Wang Shanjun 6 to 3, 6 to 4 Looking at the matches, the battle between Yang Xie Mao and Xiao Mingzu was the most dramatic. In the first game, Yang felt unfamiliar with the racket and missed opportunities in serving, so he suffered a huge blow. In the second game, Yang's energy suddenly increased and he was able to handle both positive defense and resistance with ease. He also served with power, and Xiao was unable to fight hard and eventually lost. The third game contained the nature of the final, and both sides naturally worked harder, and the ball skills were also ingenious, with constant additions and subtractions, making it difficult to distinguish between high and low. In the end, Xiao was slightly tired and was taken advantage of by the enemy and ended. However, the score had already reached 9 to 7. Results of Yesterday's Handball Singles Match 185

The all-Shanghai Chinese handball singles competition hosted by the YMCA has become increasingly serious since it started. Yesterday's Group A match between Sun Daosheng and Chen Hualu, a battle between the old and the new, was very interesting. A ball flew back and forth, and the two chased after it, with constantly changing heights and positions. Shao Jiang Chen Hualu was full of courage and his hands and feet were nimble. He was surprisingly successful and won the first game with a score of 21 to 13. In the second game, the old hero Sun Daosheng cheered up and was temporarily invincible, killing the opponent so that they could not take care of themselves and had difficulty parrying. He won back with a score of 21 to 2. The third game was a matter of life and death for the two, and both sides worked very hard, and the performance was excellent, making it impossible to not appreciate it. Sun won the final victory with a score of 21 to 8 in the third game due to his quick hands and proper handling. Wei Guanghan, the oldest in Group B, played against Wu Weizhou. Wei was the oldest in Group B. On that day, his performance was very much like an old general riding alone and invincible. Wu Weizhou tried hard to win under adverse circumstances, but it was difficult to achieve his wish. As a result, Wei won two consecutive games with a score of 20 to 13 and 21 to 14. The competition between Yang Chengcai and Lu Mengsheng in Group C was extremely intense. At first, Yang killed the opponent frequently and his momentum was great. He soon won the first game with a score of 21 to 6. However, starting from the second game, Lu showed his heroic qualities. His second-hand movement was appropriate, and he was able to cope with both sides, reversing the situation and taking a great advantage. He actually won the second and third games with a score of 21 to 17.
