Savings Department of the China Industrial Bank 223

(1) Type A Current Savings: Interest accrues at 4% per annum, compounded semi-annually. Employees and workers can deposit their monthly salaries, excluding expenses. This type of savings allows for withdrawals at any time with a check, making it superior to self-preservation.

(2) Type B Current Savings: Interest accrues at 5% per annum, compounded monthly. Children's usual scattered savings and gifts from relatives and friends can be deposited. This type of savings cultivates the virtue of saving in girls and avoids wasteful spending, achieving two goals in one stroke.

(3) Fixed Deposit Savings: Interest accrues at 8% per annum for one year and 10% per annum for two years. Public organizations such as charities and foundations for establishing schools, retirement funds for the elderly, children's education funds, and asset management entrusted by others can deposit funds, seeking a secure place to store them. The longer the deposit term, the higher the interest rate.

(4) Fixed Deposit Withdrawal Savings: Interest accrues at 7.2% per annum for two years and 9.6% per annum for fifteen years, compounded monthly. This type of savings is suitable for families where the husband is away on business and household expenses are limited and need to be paid in installments. Specify the installment withdrawal to alleviate domestic worries, avoiding delays while also earning interest.

(5) Zero Deposit Zero Withdrawal Savings: Interest accrues at 7.8% per annum for two years and 10.8% per annum for fifteen years, compounded monthly. Parents should pay attention to the needs of their children's growth, marriage, and career. Deposits made lightly and regularly in small amounts can accumulate principal and interest over time, preventing ad hoc borrowing and financial strain.

(6) Special Fixed Deposit Savings: Interest accrues at 11% per annum for fifteen years, compounded semi-annually. Those with surplus assets can deposit this type of savings, as the interest rate is most favorable, more stable than real estate, and without the risk of fire or water damage.

(7) Zero Deposit Fixed Deposit Savings: Interest accrues at 9% per annum for five years and 11.5% per annum for fifteen years, compounded semi-annually. Saving is convenient regardless of the amount. The term can be long or short, and the longer the term, the higher the interest rate.

(8) Gift Certificate Savings: Interest accrues at 5% per annum. Interest is not calculated for periods less than one month. Why spend so much on gifts that are often impractical? How about giving gift certificates, allowing the recipient to receive both principal and interest? Our certificates are printed with auspicious patterns. Please request them. Your patronage is greatly appreciated. Our bank address is No. 172 Nanjing Road. Telephone: 17835-17836.

Just a Laugh Haike 279

Dentist: *[exasperatedly]* Open your mouth wider!

Patient with toothache: I can’t open it any wider! You’re just filling a tooth, do you need to fill it from the outside or do you need to drill inside?

Father (having just beaten his young son who then bit him): How dare you bite me?

Son: Why did you hit me so hard? You don’t know how much it hurts, so I want to give you a taste of pain too.

Doctor A (arguing with another doctor over a patient): According to my diagnosis, I am sure that this medicine will cure him with one dose!

Doctor B: According to my diagnosis, I am also sure. If you don't believe me, wait until he dies and dissect him and take a look!

Patient: Please, just argue and don’t take my life!

Younger brother: Oh no, older sister, my balloon flew into the sky! What should I do?

Older sister: Don’t worry, you’re going to heaven anyway, so just wait there and play with it later!

A: You borrowed my umbrella. You need to return it today.

B: Sorry, it’s raining today, so I need to use it for another day.

A: What should I do? I don’t have an umbrella.

B: Why don’t you just borrow one from someone else like me and use it for a few more days?

A Phonetic Alphabet Incense Screen in the Words of Wu Zhirou 280

The other day, Wu Zhirou gave a speech on the phonetic alphabet at the Legislative Yuan's weekly meeting, full of humor and wit. This old gentleman's romantic charm is truly not shallow. Let's pick up a few bits to share as conversation starters.

The phonetic alphabet should be considered like incense shoes. Compared to the writing systems of Europe, America, and Japan, the phonetic alphabet currently being studied in our country is not just ten or a hundred times easier. To use the analogy of shoes that fit, those countries certainly have their own leather shoes and wooden clogs. These leather shoes and wooden clogs cannot be afforded by everyone in our country. The phonetic alphabet, however, can be compared to straw sandals. These straw sandals can be afforded by the people of our country, even those who live in remote and impoverished areas or who are so poor they have no land to stand on. Moreover, they are extremely cheap and useful. If they are deemed too simple and cannot be presented in elegant settings, it is not too late to devise methods to improve them in the future to make them refined and beautiful. Gentlemen, do not despise these humble straw sandals.

A Beauty Falls from the Sky Amidst the Sound of a Shepherd's Flute. If the phonetic alphabet can be popularized throughout the country, then even old women, servants, and shepherds can rely on it to read and write. What could be greater or more convenient than its utility? Let's talk about the scene of a shepherd tending cattle. In the setting sun, amidst fragrant grass, a shepherd boy rides backward on an ox, playing a short flute, followed by singing, "Drifting and swaying, a beauty falls from the sky." Such charm and flavor are truly difficult for ordinary people to hope to achieve. Subsequently, this can be proven by citing idioms and drawing analogies from various regions. Those who heard this could not help but burst into laughter.

On that day, Mr. Wu's speech lasted for two hours. He was full of energy and could even imagine the psychology of the audience, interspersed with anecdotes of rare foreign knowledge. It was truly rare, so it was said.

Hot Topics and Joyful Moments 281

An Elder of Over Seven Hundred Years, Ji Jin

Mr. Li from the same village returned from Southeast Asia, mentioning that in northern Borneo, there was an old man who claimed to be over seven hundred years old. His beard and hair were slightly white, and he was full of energy, looking like he was only sixty or seventy years old. People were generally skeptical of this. When asked about his methods of cultivation, his diet and clothing were no different from ordinary people's. However, he took a seawater bath every day, and he had never stopped since he was young. This is a common occurrence for those living by the sea and is not unusual. He was then asked how old his wife and children were. He replied that his wife was forty years younger than him, his oldest son was four hundred and eighty-six years old, and his youngest was three hundred and sixty-four years old. He had a new grandson fifteen years ago who was still in swaddling clothes. He added that he had children late and hoped for grandchildren very much, and their existence was a comfort to him. This kind of fantastic story made people laugh. After careful investigation, it was discovered that there was no calendar there, and the locals regarded each full moon cycle as a year. Thus, this "seven-hundred-year-old" man was not yet seventy years old. The world is so big that there is no end to wonders. This is specially recorded to support the topic.

The weather has suddenly turned hot in recent days. The sun is like a fiery umbrella hanging high in the sky during the day, with temperatures reaching over ninety degrees. Even at night, the heat is still oppressive. Therefore, cries of "It's hot!" can be heard everywhere. Here are some observations and notes taken while sweating profusely.

Strolling in the Park. This is the most fashionable and economical way to escape the heat. Therefore, although there are many parks in Shanghai, they are always crowded with visitors during the summer. Gujia Garden is especially popular. The green grass is like a carpet, and the cool breeze is refreshing. Every evening when the sun sets, walking in it is enough to make one feel refreshed and reluctant to leave. What is most envied is seeing couples sitting side by side by the pond, either teasing the fish or whispering sweet nothings. There is truly a feeling of "preferring to be mandarin ducks rather than envying immortals."

Eating Cold Foods. During the summer in Shanghai, countless temporary food stalls selling cold foods spring up. They sell nothing but soda, ice cream, and all kinds of frozen foods. Those who fear the heat flock to them, making their business extremely prosperous. Small stalls selling sour plum juice and shaved ice can also be seen everywhere on the sides of the road, catering to the needs of ordinary people.

Riding in Cars. There are also some wealthy people who take their families or lovers out for a drive in the evening. In secluded areas, they speed along, making the locals envious. However, this year, the price of gold has skyrocketed, and the price of gasoline has also increased accordingly. Therefore, those who enjoy driving for pleasure are inevitably affected to some extent.

Watching Movies. In past summers, except for open-air cinemas (the best-equipped open-air cinemas in Shanghai are the Dahua Hotel and the Paris Theatre), other movie theaters generally had slow business. However, this year is different. The theater owners have spared no effort in improving their climate control equipment. The air conditioning system installed in the Nanjing Grand Theatre is especially satisfying, and the temperature inside the theater can be reduced by fifteen degrees compared to the outside, making one feel as if they are in an ice cellar. This is also a way to escape the heat.

Jottings from a Journey, Practice 282

Trip to Jinan. The scenery of Jinan has long been famous throughout the country, and the seventy-two springs are especially scenic natural wonders. After being described by the author of "The Travels of Lao Ts'an," the black girl by Daming Lake and the beautiful scenery of Jin Mian Spring are especially unforgettable images in our imagination. After arriving in Jinan, I spent two days visiting scenic spots such as Pearl Spring, Daming Lake, Baotu Spring, and Thousand Buddha Mountain. Pearl Spring is located inside the provincial government compound and is a square pool of water. Spring water gurgles from the bottom of the pool, constantly gushing out from the gaps in the rocks. At the same time, countless bubbles rise with it, forming a string of pearls that never stop. It is truly a spectacle. What is strange is that the spring water has never dried up for thousands of years, and these continuous pearl-shaped bubbles have never stopped for even a second. It would be impossible to create this kind of miracle even with all our human effort, which shows the greatness of natural power. All I saw at Daming Lake was a patch of reeds so high that they could drown a person. There were one or two tea seats and several painted boats, but a lot of mud had accumulated on the bottom of the spring, so the area of the lake had shrunk considerably.

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia (42) Flowers 283

On the 11th, I visited the Chinese Circus, whose troupe leader, Sun Fuyou, is from Hejian. His wife is German and speaks Chinese. Sun has traveled in Europe for a long time, which is why he is fluent. The performance was quite entertaining, with seventeen horses, several large and small elephants, lions, tigers, and leopards. The elephants seemed to understand human intentions. The tigers could be played with, and even when their chains were released, they would calmly return to their cages and not try to escape. The tigers eat several pounds of beef a day, fed twice. I had seen leopards in Japan jump through flaming hoops, and Western horses were said to be able to do arithmetic. Now, these horses can also turn between four chairs without error, but it is not natural; they are directed by the whip. Bears can dance with sticks, but they always beg for food, looking very shameless. Tigers, on the other hand, would never do this. Observing the innate personalities of these animals, their inherent goodness, evil, benevolence, and violence are fixed and cannot be changed. Human nature is probably also difficult to change. Religious figures, educators, and proponents of evolution and hypnotism all say that human nature can be changed. I certainly advocate that it can be changed, but seeing how difficult it is to change the personalities of animals, I cannot help but sigh. In Nanjing, I watched a tiger eat a chicken, starting from the legs and eating up to the head, then discarding the chicken while it was still alive. I watched it with my family and felt sorry for the chicken. But elephants naturally beg for food, and tigers naturally eat meat. These inherent natures are difficult to change, so how can there be equality? I take full responsibility for those who want to transform society. I have two methods for this. First, we must use eugenics to prevent inferior breeds and criminals from reproducing. Second, we must use hypnotism. If all else fails, we must resort to surgery on those who cause chaos to achieve peace. Complaining about the environment is useless if human nature cannot be changed.

On the 11th, Mr. Lu Weichang of the Jingwu Association invited me to see the Chinese martial arts performance of the circus. The troupe is jointly organized by the Jingwu Association and is quite large, with about seventy or eighty people. They have traveled from Guangdong to Annam, Siam, Singapore, and are about to go to the Dutch colonies to tour America. Their tent can hold three or four thousand people and is very flexible to set up. When not in use, it can be rolled up and carried to other cities. The interior is four or five fathoms high, and the electric lights are as bright as day, and it is not afraid of rain. It imitates European designs. European circuses constantly tour and perform in various places. Women perform martial arts on a tightrope. Westerners applaud when they see it, and they especially like how they can do somersaults from a height of four or five fathoms without falling. People are surprised and do not understand how they can be so good. Also, Mr. Sun can hold a pole more than two fathoms long on his head, and a child performs various acts on top of the pole while Sun moves freely below. This act is very dangerous. Afterward, Mr. Sun threw flying knives made of wooden chips. They flew in a circle of three or four fathoms and returned to his hand. The audience was very surprised, realizing that this was the same as the flying knives of swordsmen, but made of thin iron sheets. There are many extraordinary people with skills in the world, but it is a pity that we cannot see them more often. According to people, Western circuses teach animals more advanced tricks than Eastern circuses, and they can perform various movements. Eastern circuses, on the other hand, excel in human skills more than Western circuses. Mr. Lu is generous and extremely gentle. His theory of boxing returns to gentleness, so he highly approves of my theory of softening. He said that he should spend 100,000 yuan to buy an airplane to travel the world to promote female transformation and pacifism to stop killing. When he was in Siam, Xiao Fucheng gave him a poem and praised him as a "roaming knight of the divine land."

There are few tourists here. Not only is it impossible to find the drum book venues described in "The Travels of Lao Ts'an," but even the pavilion in front of the railing where people urinate, as described in "A Marriage to Awaken the World," is nowhere to be seen. There are only two or three boats. The area of the lake is so small that it is not as good as the back lake of Nanjing, which allows for paddling and leisurely enjoyment. Therefore, we quickly looked at it and felt bored. The next day, the scenery of Thousand Buddha Mountain was quite similar to Jiming Temple in Nanjing. Climbing the mountain and looking out over the entire city of Jinan, the city streets and houses are clearly visible, which is quite exhilarating. I wrote two couplets to show a glimpse. (1) "Springs gush from the earth, peaks surge, the land of Tanzi has an atmosphere, the seas and mountains are suitable for Du Fu's poetry." This couplet describes the scenery and also mentions the scenery. It is hung in the main hall of Xingguo Temple on Thousand Buddha Mountain. (2) "All forms are empty, cities, mountains, and rivers are like illusions, clouds and smoke pass before the eyes, the wealth and nobility of immortals leave no trace." This couplet can express our feelings when visiting mountains. It is hung in the front hall, and the rest are not worth watching. The so-called Thousand Buddha Mountain is a cave formed by the Jianyan cliff, with dozens of Buddha statues enshrined inside. This was added by later generations, and its original intention must have been different.

Jinan's weather combines the strengths of both north and south, not dry, not cold, not blowing strong winds, without long-lasting rain, the soil is yellow, and the water is very clear. Since the commercial port has prospered, the roads are quite tidy, and the market has a prosperous appearance. From my perspective, the various advantages of Jinan as the provincial capital surpass those of Nanjing.

News from the publishing industry. The Drama Monthly, edited by Mr. Liu Huogong of the Datong Bookstore, the tenth issue of the second volume, was published yesterday morning. It includes inscriptions by Sun Juxian, Ru Fuhui, Tiangang Shi, Zhou Chuan'ying, stage photos of Mei Lanfang, Shang Xiaoyun, Xun Huisheng, Zhang Wenyan, Wang Huilan, Hu Bilan, Yang Juqiu, Guo Jiyun, and others, "Pear Dimples Tidbits" by Zhang Cixi, "Notes on Listening to Music" by Feng Xiaoyin, the play script "Peach Blossom Village" by Hao Shouchen, "Golden Lock Record" by Cheng Yanqiu, and "Su Wu Herding Sheep" by Wang Fengqing, and dozens of articles on drama theory. It can be said to be a perfect compilation.

Warmth in My Heart (2) (2) (7) Bao Tianxiao 284

Chapter 12: Farewell Banquet, Holding Flowers to Leave a Beautiful Impression, Garden Gathering, Tea Tasting to See the Fragrant Posture

Among them were one or two philanthropists who had returned from abroad and had new ideas. They often encountered charitable relief societies abroad and saw that the wives and daughters of the upper class were always in charge. When these noblewomen came out to advocate, everyone would come to help. This is called "when you climb high and call, the mountains respond," which can achieve twice the result with half the effort. Although we have not had this kind of charitable relief society in China, the ladies in Shanghai are now much more open-minded than before. Taking the matter of foot-binding as an example, although the ladies in their thirties suffered from this customary pain from childhood, and many of their golden lotuses were unable to be unbound, they had to think of the next best thing, which was to wear round-toed, flat-bottomed shoes, or stuff a large piece of cotton into the toes of their shoes to make a pair of fake big feet, like the natural feet of girls of thirteen, fourteen, fifteen, or sixteen years old, which were also in the majority. Having suffered from the pain of foot-binding themselves, they would not allow their beloved daughters to suffer this pain again. Secondly, the number of girls studying in girls' schools opened by foreigners is gradually increasing. Chinese people advocate female education, and the number of female students in girls' schools run by themselves is also increasing year by year. There are even female bachelors who have graduated from abroad. It can be seen that the ladies of China are gradually moving towards openness. So why can't we open this kind of charitable relief society? He also thought that Shanghai is an international trading port, and if foreigners were involved in everything, things would be much more convenient. Those ladies living in Shanghai originally felt too idle, and they were very happy to be recruited to cooperate. In our association, there should be at least one or two wives of consuls or three or four mistresses of big bosses of foreign companies. Then the matter would be successful, and the momentum would be great. They have run such associations in their own countries, so they are naturally experts. Then the Chinese ladies, who have never run such an association, would naturally be guided by them and could become a respectable association. Of course, this matter must obtain the consent of the foreign ladies. Secondly, we need to think about the address for the meeting. There is no such big place in Shanghai owned by Chinese people. Borrowing a place from foreigners is not very decent. After all, it is for the charitable cause of the Chinese people. After thinking and thinking, I thought of Zhang's Garden. Only Zhang's Garden is a place owned by us Chinese people and is barely suitable. There is a lawn in the back that can be temporarily set up with many tents or reed sheds, like a garden party. By then, after decoration and with the electric lights shining brightly, it would look like a brocade of flowers. At this time, we must discuss with the owner of Zhang's Garden and get his permission.

Gold Standard Speculation Hidden Reversal 285

The trend was peaceful, hovering within the pass. Yesterday's (4th) gold standard situation was still stable, but the hidden softening had already shown signs of reversal. The previous market had five taels of small money, with twists and turns. The after-market only had a three-tael turnover, but the people's sentiment hidden within the 600 tael mark was stable. Foreign exchange slightly weakened, and the listed prices were unchanged. Inter-bank transactions were not frequent, and the cash flow of various firms was normal. Firms such as Yuancheng, Fuchang, Zhifengyong, etc., all made purchases, while Hengxing, Yuanmao, Yongtai, Kangrunyuan, Kangxiang, etc., mostly sold. However, the de-inventory was slow and unreliable. In the early market, the big bar suddenly saw a rebound and immediately broke through the 600 tael mark because of large household chasing. Sellers did not relent, and buyers retreated, making it difficult to sustain. The wind turned downward, and there was a sharp drop of more than five taels. At noon, it slightly picked up by two or three taels. In the after-market, various firms went in and out from time to time, and the price softened, with fluctuations of one or two taels. Finally, it stood outside 597 taels. The trend of foreign exchange bills was peaceful. Yesterday, British silver bars increased by one-sixteenth, and the price of silver also increased by one-quarter.

A short-lived surge then faltered. The opening price for August immediately fell by four taels and six qian, to 597 taels and three qian. The gross turnover fluctuated by two or three taels, retreating from 97 taels and eight qian to five taels and eight qian. An announcement was made not to move people's hearts, and it seemed good. Therefore, it reached 99 taels to 9 taels and five qian, and the internal situation was stable. The Bank of Japan bought one tael, three qian, four fen, three, seven, five, and recently one tael, three qian, four fen, half zhengjin absorbed six pence, two, five of British gold. Shanghai's monthly subscription was 36 yuan, five, six, two, five. At noon, it was sixty-six taels.

The evening closed down four taels and six qian. The after-market opened at 97 taels and seven qian, then dropped from seven taels and nine qian to seven taels and two qian. Then, because retail investors bought in, it rebounded by more than one tael to 98 taels, six or seven qian. Because the Indian exchange rebounded, the people's sentiment seemed to be frustrated. At one fifteen, it was 97 taels and two qian. Suddenly, it was heard that the bank had taken in September British gold at six pence, one, eight, seven, five. HSBC and Datong did the following month's six pence, one, two, five, and Hengxing, etc., bought in, so it jumped up by two taels. Around three o'clock, it was 99 taels and a half. After a while, the sellers were still not quiet and retreated by three taels to 96 taels, five or six qian. Hedging bars also came to sell. Immediately, it rose by more than two taels again. Hengxing, etc., entered again. After three thirty, it was 99 taels. Then, Hengxing suddenly sold out, and the market atmosphere suddenly weakened. After four o'clock, it was seven taels and one qian. By four thirty, it was 97 taels and two qian, a decrease of four taels and six qian compared to the day before. Foreign Exchange Also Turned Loose and Discounted 286

Very Little Cash Flow from Chinese Merchants

Yesterday, HSBC's foreign exchange listed prices did not change at all. However, the banks' buy and sell prices seemed to have loosened and discounted. From the early morning, it weakened and then stabilized. At noon, it loosened again. There was not much good or bad in the afternoon. Sino-Foreign Cotton Yarn: Demand from Sichuan and Guangdong Remains Strong

Actual sales of cotton yarn are gradually picking up. Buyers from Sichuan and Guangdong continue to make purchases with relatively strong interest, which has somewhat strengthened market confidence. However, the overseas market for cotton yarn remains weak. Therefore, Indian and Japanese merchants are taking short positions during price increases. The majority sentiment in the market is that with the approaching autumn season, yarn sales are expected to improve. Additionally, there are widespread rumors of yarn factories stopping night shifts (although most factories are still profitable). Therefore, the current market tightness is difficult to reverse in the short term. If actual sales continue steadily, another increase of 1 or 2% is possible.

Open Bidding Prices Fluctuate: Human Bidding

The market opened with near-month contracts slightly down. As the bidding reached the far-month contracts, market sentiment stagnated. Large transactions occurred with second and third grade yarns for customer sales, which intensified market anxiety. As a result, prices for all months increased by 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.4, and 0.5 yuan. In the afternoon, news of large purchases of spot yarn by Guangdong and Sichuan further strengthened market confidence, causing the opening price to jump by 0.4 or 0.5 yuan. A telegram regarding third-grade yarn caused a drop of 2 yuan, leading to a sudden market decline of 0.5 to 0.7 yuan. Ultimately, near-month contracts increased by 0.2 to 0.4 yuan, while far-month contracts decreased by 0.1, 0.4, and 0.5 yuan. The total trading volume for the day was 14,700 bales. Sellers included Yu Da, Mao Ji, Shen Chang, Xin Cheng, Chang Feng, Yi Long, and Yi Cheng, selling from 300 to 850 bales. Buyers included Yi Yu, Rong Xing, Tian Cheng, Da Chang Cheng, Shen Xin, and Da Feng, buying from 350 to 950 bales. The closing prices for human bidding are recorded on the left.

American Cotton Cooperative Buys July Contracts Again 292

Market activity seems to be awaiting the new cotton crop situation.

A telegram from New York on the 3rd reported on the cotton market situation for the week: Trading on the cotton exchange has been very quiet this week, with only slight price fluctuations. There has been some short covering and some retail buying, reportedly due to high temperatures in the South and dry weather in central cotton belt regions and the northern border of Texas. The cooperative has also bought July contracts. It is rumored that the cooperative has taken delivery of a total of 170,000 bales of July contracts before the cutoff date. It is unknown how the cotton stockpiled by the cooperative will be sold in the future, but the cooperative has stated that it will not sell in a market with weak buying interest. Cotton merchants are now gradually becoming more bullish, but large-scale buying will only occur if there is a reduction in trade activity or a reduction in the new cotton crop.

Furthermore, there was little trading in the market due to the upcoming national holiday and the government's release of the cotton acreage report on Tuesday. Therefore, some short covering occurred. Demand and sales of cotton, as well as trade in piece goods, are not strong. The weather is still good, and the cotton crop is progressing well.

Estimates of American Cotton Consumption and Carryover 293

The New York Cotton Exchange estimates that world consumption of American cotton this season will be 13.2 million to 13.4 million bales. The worldwide American cotton carryover as of July 31st is estimated to be 5.8 million to 6 million bales.

American Private Cotton Acreage Estimate 294

A telegram from New York on the 3rd reported that the Foscue Bureau in Tennessee estimates this year's cotton acreage to be 45,775,000 acres.

Grain Shipments Obstructed, Flour Prices Plunge 295

All months fell by about 0.03 yuan.

Yesterday, the flour market was still firm in each month, with domestic traders maintaining a positive outlook, leading to a slight increase compared to the previous day's closing price. However, the market atmosphere suddenly changed dramatically in the afternoon, shifting from enthusiastic to bleak. The reason for the price decline was that the spot flour being shipped by Tianjin traders was suddenly blocked by customs for export, causing shippers to cancel their declarations (it is rumored that all grains and daily necessities are also prohibited). After this news spread, there was widespread panic, with the assumption that northern sales would be halted and that demand for flour would be difficult to develop for the time being. Under such circumstances, the market situation immediately faltered. Therefore, the current month's price opened at 0.25 yuan, a sharp drop of 0.035 yuan from the morning closing price. August and September also fell sharply at the same time. Subsequently, as long positions were sold off, market sentiment turned consistently bearish, and the market continued to decline. After observing the situation, it is likely that the decline will continue. Ultimately, August fell by 0.03 yuan compared to the previous day, September fell by 0.03 yuan, October fell by 0.02 yuan, November fell by 0.02 yuan, and December fell by 0.02 yuan.

Wheat Futures Follow Flour Downstream 296

Over 2,000 bags of spot wheat were traded.

Yesterday, the wheat futures market was generally flat, with only slight fluctuations compared to the previous day. However, the market atmosphere changed in the afternoon due to the suspension of flour exports. There was widespread speculation that flour sales would become more sluggish, and the need for wheat would also decrease. Therefore, sentiment for both near and far-term contracts inevitably softened. Originally, various factories had been thinking of lowering prices due to high costs, but now, taking advantage of this opportunity, the pressure to sell seemed to increase. As a result, the current month's price fell by 0.03 yuan compared to the previous day, August fell by 0.05 yuan, September fell by 0.04 yuan, October fell by 0.04 yuan, November fell by 0.02 yuan, and December fell by 0.01 yuan. Spot wheat prices reflected the fact that various factories were holding firm and unwilling to lower prices. Yesterday, 2,000 bags of wheat from various stores such as Hezhou, Shuangfeng, Shashi, Baoying, Pukou, and Zhenjiang were opened, and were purchased separately by small and medium-sized factories.

River Rice Increasingly Quiet 297

Yesterday, no rice boats arrived in Zhabei from the river. All registered stockpiled goods were subject to the risk of discoloration and heat damage due to the fluctuating weather. Therefore, there was an urgent need for assessment to avoid losses. However, the price assessment bureau still had over 1,000 bags of rice that rice shops had not claimed. Some of this rice had been assessed during rainy weather, so there was also an urgent need for shops to pay and collect it. Unfortunately, very few people came to claim it. Therefore, river rice assessment had to be delayed slightly, and the situation was quiet. Indicia rice was unavailable, and Meta rice became more sluggish. Market prices remained stable.

There was no arrival of Shanghai Northern or Southern Japonica rice. The exchange of Indicia Meta was slight and business was slow, and large plate sales were deadlocked. There was temporarily no distinction between Yangdu and Jian rice grades, with only slight increases or decreases for higher grades. Yesterday, there were also good reports on foreign rice, which bolstered market confidence. There was some inquiry in the main street, but due to the scarcity of goods, the situation remained unchanged.

Another report stated that recently, the price of Japonica rice in this port had soared to 24 yuan, but after the authorities limited it to 21 yuan, most traders from inner roads stopped shipping to Shanghai. Therefore, the stockpile of broken Japonica rice in the hinterland was slightly thicker. The recent harvest is right in the middle of the season of rice hulling and whitening, and every year most of the rice is shipped to Shanghai for sale at this time. However, after Shanghai’s market came to a standstill, except for a few goods merchants shipping to other ports and selling them elsewhere, the rest were all watching or preparing to stop hulling the Japonica rice, since unpolished rice is difficult to store for a long time. However, according to investigations, each rice shop in this port still has more than a month’s worth of stock, so there is no urgency to purchase more. In addition, Eastern new Japonica rice can be launched in the middle of the eighth month of the national calendar, and new Indica rice from the Southern and Western routes can also be seen on schedule, so the domestic goods merchants are gradually panic-stricken. Once the new goods are on the market, people will inevitably change, and the stagnation of Chen Japonica rice will be eliminated. This year’s Eastern new Japonica rice harvest is better than in previous years, so it is predicted that the price of rice after a month may turn sharply downwards.

Zhejiang Summer Cocoons Are Only 30% of the Year's Total 299

At most, no more than 12,000 to 13,000 bales of dried cocoons are transported to Shanghai.

Although the amount of summer silkworms raised in Zhejiang, Hangzhou, Shaoxing, Huzhou, Jiaxing, and other places was smooth this year, they have been damaged by uneven weather, losing 60% to 70% of the crop. The amount of fresh cocoons produced is only about 30% of the usual yield. The cocoon market is coming to an end, and dried cocoons are piled up at various stations, awaiting urgent transport. Silk cocoon merchants are trying to get railway authorities to allocate cars. It is estimated that the total amount of summer dried cocoons transported to Shanghai from Zhejiang this year will be no more than 12,000 to 13,000 bales.

The Russian trading house is about to open.

Amid the slump in the tea market, since the director of the Russian Cooperative Association came to Shanghai to prepare for the resumption of business, Chinese and foreign tea merchants have paid special attention. The tea market has turned around, and the cooperative's foreign firm has been actively busy with internal arrangements and reviewing tea samples from various routes. According to news from the Russian side, the company plans to hold an opening ceremony for Gongxi tea and Shangzhou and Hubei patterned black tea next week. Although Zhenmei and Qihong tea are not urgently needed, telegrams have been sent to merchants for consideration. In light of the imminent opening of the Russian trading house, merchants in Wudong, Tunzhuang, and Gongxi began actively searching for supplies, and the market price suddenly increased by 10 taels. However, the market for green teas such as Zhenmei and Zhenmei, and Qimen black tea, remains unchanged.

Among the prizes are high-legged gramophones and Kodak cameras, which are displayed in the company's doors and windows, welcoming visitors from all walks of life.

Sanxing Shoes and Hats Store, located behind Qingtianbao Silver Building in Xiaodongmen, claims that their store has been established for decades. Due to business development, another branch has been set up on the newly developed Dongmen Road, specializing in the production of trendy and newly designed shoes, women's shoes, and children's shoes, as well as selling silk stockings, thread socks, and various cosmetics. A special grand prize will be given out for one month starting today (the 5th) on the day of the opening.

Penglai Cafe claims that its restaurant is newly located in the Penglai Market in South Shanghai, specializing in the production of ice cream, shaved ice, fruit dew, and various frozen cold foods, which are all available. In the midst of the scorching summer heat, it is very popular with ladies, and the business is extremely prosperous, with a great influx of people. This is because the products are exquisite and the pricing is low, and the seating is exquisite and the service is attentive. Now, after a survey by the Health Bureau, it is considered that the products are very hygienic and are promoted as the number one cold food restaurant in South Shanghai.

The Zhonghua Department Store at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Central Zhejiang Road claims that since the beginning of this month, although there has been continuous rain and wind, the business is still not bad. Yesterday, the weather was fine and the crowding of customers was unprecedented since the opening. The goods that are most popular with customers are printed silk for 0.5 yuan per foot, women's silk stockings for 0.4 yuan per pair, and seasonal straw hats for 0.8 yuan per piece.

Theater News 307

The New Central Grand Theater announces that the Shanghai Film Company's production, "Tofu Xishi," directed by Du Yu and starring Yin Mingzhu, will premiere at the New Central Theater starting today (the 5th). Yin Mingzhu delivers a novel and exceptional performance in this film, captivating and amusing audiences alike. Both day and night showings will feature new and romantic erotic dance programs from the Shanghai Girls' Erotic Dance Troupe, including "My Love," "Butterfly Girl," and "Butterfly Lovers," offering delightful songs and graceful dances to please the eyes and ears, and alleviate any emotional distress. The Jiande Savings Society proclaims that since its reorganization, the Peking Opera Department has become highly efficient. In addition to inviting the renowned opera expert, Mr. Su Shaoqing, to serve as an honorary advisor, they have also hired veteran performers Mr. Feng Zihe and Mr. Cheng Yuzhang as permanent instructors. Consequently, the department's affairs are progressing rapidly and exceptionally. It is announced that the department is scheduled to hold a dress rehearsal at 6:00 PM on July 5th in the society's auditorium. The program includes "Hou Wenjun and Zhong Wenbin's Doing Good Deeds Leads to Having a Son," "Xia Lianfu and Zhu Zhulin, Xiang Yun Guan Master's Earl's Party Seeks a Bride," "Wu Junheng's Jin Dian Zhuang Feng (Feigning Madness in the Golden Palace)," "Lu Shaoan and Zhu Shiliang's Cao Fu Ascends to Immortality," "Feng Manyuan's Chunxiang Disturbing the School," "Zhang Xide and Cheng Yuzhang's Righteous Alliance," "Cao Xuanqing's Su San Qi Jie (Su San Escorted for Trial)," "Tang Yunqing guest-starring in Zou's Fourth Son Visiting His Mother," "Dai Baocheng's Empress Dowager He Ascends the Throne," and "Lu Shaoan, Zhang Xide, Yin Zhongqin, and Guo Yichi's Crossing the River for a Feast," and so on. It is anticipated that the event will add a unique brilliance to the dramatic arts. "Qiu Bo Yuan" (Autumn Waves of Resentment) is an American film originally titled "Smiling Irish Eyes." It premieres today (the 5th) at the Odeon Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road. We are informed that its special characteristic is that American films seem to be emphasizing the ethnic or regional backgrounds of the leading actors. Indeed, American films have started to focus on depicting the actors' cultural and regional origins. For example, if Clara Bow is starring in a film this year, she often portrays her own regional culture from New York, and because she embodies the robust beauty of the modern American woman, she is usually cast in films depicting modern American life, such as "Wild Party" and "Good Sisters." Similarly, Dolores del Río, a Mexican beauty who went to Hollywood only a few years ago and hasn't acted in many films, is cast by Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer in films showcasing her own Mexican culture because she is Mexican. That film is called "The Bad One." But this particular trait is especially evident in the film "Autumn Waves of Resentment" that I want to introduce. As readers know, the lead actress, Colleen Moore, is of Irish descent. With an Irish beauty playing in a film with an Irish cultural background, the display of national spirit and the vividness of the regional color are naturally more authentic than, say, an American actor playing a French count. Moreover, Miss Colleen Moore is a qualified actress. The story goes like this: In a place in Ireland, due to the beauty of the scenery, a passionate man and a passionate girl grow up. The man loves music and plays the violin skillfully. The girl has a natural singing voice, and in the shade of the setting sun, she often sings like a oriole. Therefore, they are brought together by their shared love of art and their proximity. Whenever the setting sun reflects on the clear stream and the gentle breeze rustles through the flowers, they exchange warm feelings through song and strings. Their hearts resonate, and their feelings become uncontrollable. They embrace, lean on each other, and kiss. However, the path of life is always somewhat bumpy. That is to say, a drama needs conflict. So, into their peaceful and elegant life comes a third party, forming a love triangle. This love triangle disrupts the peace and elegance, adding much bitterness and sorrow, and much excitement and grief. The man's violin is smashed by the third party, indirectly breaking the girl's heart. However, a broken heart can be mended, and deep affection is the magic cure. A beauty cannot be forced, and the fruit of love is a weapon against stubborn enemies. Therefore, the girl shows anger and haughtiness towards the man's rival, but smiles and tenderness towards the man. This smile and tenderness in her eyes give the film its name. What follows is the sadness of separation and heartbreak, but tenderness remains tenderness. Although tears may flow, a smile is still offered, creating a symbol of life. The narrative of the film is that simple, but because of the strong regional flavor, it vividly expresses the Irish national spirit, evoking emotions and inner resonance in the viewers. Moreover, the clever director sometimes brings us to America amidst the gentle and exciting scenes, allowing us to enjoy the exotic charm of modern American life. Colleen Moore puts in great effort in this film, using her unique eye expressions throughout. She is inherently cute like a little bird, never being pretentious or overly enthusiastic, always maintaining her liveliness and innocence. What makes her especially endearing are the smiles in her eyes and on her lips, and the innocent charm of a young girl. In short, although she is a married woman, she is still like a child. In short, she is Irish. (Zhu Ben)

The Story of World Literature (1) (7) (5) by American Harnish, translated by Hu Zhongchi

Chapter 46: Scandinavian Literature 309

Modern Norwegian literature can be divided into three eras: the pioneers, the Ibsen era, and the new movement. The pioneers were the two poets Wergeland and Welhaven. Although neither of them did anything individually, Wergeland can be called the founder of Norwegian literature. He was an energetic and enthusiastic poet, an eloquent revolutionary, and can be described as the northern Rousseau. However, he never perfected his style, and his obscurity and obstinacy harmed his teachings and his ideas. Some of his lyric poems are extremely beautiful. After a busy career, he died young. Welhaven was a conservative, a champion of clarity and order. He attacked Wergeland's licentiousness with vigorous pamphlets. His struggle for stability and clarity had a beneficial influence on Norwegian thought and style. His authority is still great today, because he was above petty criticism. He was a poet, and his poems on ancient Norwegian themes established him as a classic of Norwegian literature. The Ibsen era includes Bjørnson, Jonas Lie, and Kielland. Kielland was a novelist with first-rate talent. Among the two, Lie was the more powerful writer. He was the leading novelist of the time. His first major work, "The Pilot and His Wife," made him the undisputed head of Norwegian novels. His novels were widely read at home and gained great fame abroad. Several of them have been translated into English. "One of Life's Slaves," "The Barque Future," and "Niobe" are his strengths. His strength does not lie in tense and amazing scenes, but in his calm observation of ordinary people. Ibsen is the greatest playwright of the past 150 years. No playwright in any country can doubt his prominence. In the world of dramatic literature, he is on par with Aeschylus, Shakespeare, and Corneille. This is not an attempt to compare them, but to show greatness. His plays are divided into two types: lyrical romantic and realistic. Poetic dramas mostly belong to the early period, while prose dramas belong to the later period. Among the poetic dramas are "Brand" and "Peer Gynt," which raised Norwegian literature to the level of the best literature in Europe. "Peer Gynt" is a fantastic satire that applies not only to the Norwegian people but also to universal humanity. It is a world classic, and its greatness is confirmed by Grieg's magnificent music. Ibsen's first realistic prose drama is "A Doll's House," in which a woman advocates for her own rights, rebelling against the old idea that a wife is a slave to her husband. This was discussed throughout Europe. Although "feminist liberation theory" is now an old story and much of the literature on the subject has faded, Ibsen's plays still have vitality. His next play, which aroused people's emotions, is "Ghosts," which explores the heredity of disease. This play has become somewhat outdated due to physiological inaccuracies. It received fierce attacks, and Ibsen retaliated fiercely with a play called "An Enemy of the People." Ibsen is often seen as a problem-seeker and a propagandist aiming to improve society. He actually has no such intention, just as he has no intention of opening a medical school or founding a new religion. He was originally a playwright who focused on dramatic effect. He only paid attention to society because society provided him with materials. This is clear in "Rosmersholm," where the problem is simply dramatic: the struggle between a weak man and a strong woman. Moreover, if the protagonist is played by an actress like Nazimova, it is a striking play. This is also clear in "Hedda Gabler." In "Hedda Gabler," there is no social issue, only personal entanglements. In his later plays, he became a poet again, not with the poetry of his youth, but with a symbolic approach based on keen thinking. This can be seen most clearly in "The Master Builder" and in the wonderful play "When We Dead Awaken," which ended his career. All of his plays have been translated into English by William Archer. Those who like spicy flavors and sound criticism will want to read a small book by another playwright, G. Bernard Shaw, called "The Quintessence of Ibsenism." Ibsen concentrated all his thoughts on poetry, drama, and the theater. His contemporary, Bjørnson, who was less talented, scattered his energy not only on all forms of literature but also on the complex political sphere. He excelled in novels and never surpassed his early stories of peasant life. "Arne" and "A Happy Boy" made him famous in many countries, just like Ibsen. He had practical knowledge of the stage, having served as the manager of the Christiania Theater. His plays are full of action and speed, and have many beautiful poetic sections where the author is not too impatient. His heroic plays based on Icelandic legends, "Sigurd Slembe" and "Sigurd Jorsalfare," place him among the great poets of the century. His comedies are interesting, and he has more humor than Ibsen, or at least more cheerful humor. His dual qualification as a poet and a political reformer led him to be criticized as a rebel. His passionate republicanism reminds us of George Sand. Ibsen, Bjørnson, and Lie were long-lasting and, even after their physical deaths, still guiding literary figures. However, younger people have arrived. Garborg, the son of a farmer, wrote novels in the farmers' dialect. He was not noticed until he wrote the startling work "Tired Men" in ordinary language. A delicate and excellent romantic novelist is Thomas Krag. His most famous novel is "Ada Wilde." A writer who is famous in his country and has recently been well received in English translation is Bojer, who combines romance and satire. However, the towering figure in the recent Norwegian novel scene is Hamsun. He has written forty novels, many of which are masterpieces. "Hunger" and "Growth of the Soil" are especially notable. He depicts the difficult side of life -- the word "vulgar" is not suitable here -- and he depicts it deeply. However, his depth is purifying and antiseptic. More importantly, he writes with a beauty that can be glimpsed in translation. Swedish literature has a long history, like Danish and Norwegian literature, which did not begin at any definite time. However, this tedious definition is possible: when Gustavus Adolphus revived the country to its highest military and political development in the seventeenth century, literature, which had been stagnant in the sixteenth century, began to flourish. In the same century, there was at least one great writer, Stiernhielm, the "father of Swedish poetry," who felt that his native language was rough and made it smooth, adopting many poetic forms. Another poet, Rosenhane, brought the Renaissance to Sweden with many short poems based on French models. During the eighteenth century, Sweden was a follower of French and English intellectuals in both prose and poetry. We do not see any great names in literature there, but there is one great name, although outside our field, that is not redundant to mention here: Linnaeus, the first genius in botany. As in other countries, in the eighteenth century, the Swedish literary ideal was academic and formal, but without the genius of the French and English pedants. And as in all countries, in Sweden, too, there was a reaction against the pedants at the beginning of the nineteenth century. The romantics were ultimately victorious. In the Swedish romantic movement, there was a great poet, Tegnér. In 1835, Longfellow, who was studying in Sweden, wrote, "Sweden has one great poet, and only one, and that is Tegnér." Longfellow's translations of Tegnér are interesting, poetic, and cleverly arranged with rhythm. Like most romantics, Tegnér saw rich material in the past, in the legends of his ancestors. His main work is "Frithiof's Saga," which spread his fame throughout Europe and earned him the position of bishop, which was completely unsuitable for him. Correction: The last paragraph of yesterday's article was misprinted as the end of the paragraph. This is a correction.
